“tirukkuRaL” English translation by Ramachandra dikshitar

Source:
Tirukkural of Tiruvalluvar (in Roman transliteration)
with English Translation
by
V.R. Ramachandra Dikshitar, M.A.,
Professor of Indian History and Archaeology, University of Madras

with a Foreword by
Sir A. Ramaswami Mudaliar, Dewan of Mysore

The Adyar Library, 1949
(The Adyar Library Series Nr. 67)

Price Rs. 3
Printed by C.Subbarayudu at the Vasanta Press,
The Theosophical Society, Adyar, Madras

FOREWORD

It has been long my desire to get an English translation in simple language of the holy Tirukkural, the teachings of which, to Tamilians, are an eternal inspiration and guide. More than 25 years back, I had invoked the aid and assistance of a great Tamil Pandit with whose collaboration I felt I would be in a position to bring out such a translation but, owing to his untimely demise, I had to give up the project. The happy thought struck me a few years back that, if my esteemed friend, Professor V. R. Ramachandra Dikshitar, could under take this task, it would be the consummation of my hope and desire. Professor Ramachandra Dikshitar readily agreed to my request that he might undertake to translate the holy Tirukkural. I could not have entrusted the work to a more distinguished scholar of Tamil literature or a better writer of simple and elegant English. Mr. Dikshitar’s contribution in research, particularly of Tamil literature, is well known and needs no emphasis.

Mr. Dikshitar has presented to the public two volumes of the Tirukkural, one containing the text in Tamil with the English translation and the other, the text in Roman transliteration with the same English translation. I hope and trust that these volumes will have a wide circulation both in India and outside and that it will be possible, by donations and subsidy, to issue these volumes at a comparatively small cost. There is a great deal of patriotism in South India for Tamil language and a legitimate pride exhibited in the eternal verities that are enshrined in this holy scripture. This patriotism and pride will have to manifest itself by providing facilities for spreading these great divine truths to as wide a populace as possible, thereby extending that knowledge to races and peoples whose mother tongue is not Tamil. Tamil is one of the most ancient of classics and yet, while other classical literature has been translated into many of the modern languages, Tamil classics have been retained as the sole proud possession of Tamil scholars and have rarely been translated into other languages, Indian or foreign.
Now that Mr. Dikshitar has completed his task, it behoves all of us who are enthusiastic about the Tamil language and more, about its literature, to do our best to make it available to peoples in foreign countries. I should like to express my very sincere thanks to Mr. Dikshitar for acceding to my request and bringing out these publications.

A. RAMASWAMI MUDALIAR
CARLTON HOUSE,
Bangalore, 15th May 1949

PREFATORY NOTE

This is the first time that the Adyar Library has included a Tamil text in its Series. The name of Prof. V. R. Ramachandra Dikshitar, the editor and translator of the Tirukkural now published, is already well-known as a great Tamil scholar by his book on The Studies in Tamil Literature and History. He is the well known Translator of that difficult Tamil classic the Silappadikaram. A smaller book of his, The Origin and spread of the Tamils, has already been published in this Series as No. 58 in 1947. It is a matter of gratification to the Library to be able to publish one of the most important Tamil Classics with an English translation by such a great scholar in the Library Series.

There may be many students who would be able to read and to study this text if it could be made available in a script with which they are familiar. And the Roman script is now fairly well spread over in the whole world; that is why the text has been given in the Roman script, with the English translation. But we cannot ignore the big population that knows the Tamil script, and the text in the Roman script may not be known to them to the same extent, if at all they know it. So there is given a parallel volume of the text in Tamil script with the same English translation as No. 68.

The Tirukkural is in three parts, dealing with the three “Aims” in life, namely, Dharma, Artha and Kama, so well-known in Hindu thought. We hear more now-a-days about the Varnasramadharma, as the foundation of Hindu life. But the real basis of Hindu life is the Trivarga, the three-fold objects of life, dealt with in this text. Perhaps the expression Puruşarthacatuştaya, (the four-fold objects of life) is more popular, with Moksa or final release as the fourth. But the truth is that according to the true Hindu view the objects of life are only three, and the fourth comes as a natural sequence. The three objects of life are not mutually exclusive; it is only a question of importance according to the different tendencies of the individuals.

The text and the translation are given one against the other on opposite pages, so that one can very easily make use of the translation while reading the text. The text has been edited before, and a few commentaries too are known. There have been also English translations prior to this. But the value of this new translation will be clear to anyone who reads the book. The text in Roman transliteration is now appearing for the first time. To the scholarship of Prof. Dikshitar is added the fame of the Vasanta Press for neat printing; and such a wealth is now offered at a very moderate price by the Adyar Library which has always sacrificed profit in the interest of service.

ADYAR LIBRARY C. KUNHAN RAJA
13th April, 1949
(New Year Day)

PREFACE

MORE than four years ago Sir A. Ramaswami Mudaliar, now Dewan of Mysore, suggested that I might undertake a translation of the Tirukkural as also its transliteration. The present book is the outcome of his suggestion. To serve the needs of a wider public, it is now published in two volumes, one containing the text in Roman transliteration and the other in Tamil script, and both containing English translation. The Tirukkural of Tiruvalluvar is the pride of South India. What the Bhagavad Gita is to the Sanskritist, the Tirukkural is to the lover of Tamil. In this book Tiruvalluvar treats of Muppal, or Trivarga (Dharma, Artha, and Kama). He has divided his book into three parts, the first dealing with Aram, the second with Porul, and the last with Kāma. This Tamil classic deals in extenso with the moral values of life which foster neighbourliness and love among all men and women to whatever race or community they may belong. It is now nearly twenty years since I published my Studies in Tamil Literature and History, where I have assigned the first or second century B. C. as the date of its composition. I find no reason to change that view.

In this endeavour I have largely followed the text and consulted the translation of the Tirukkural published by Sri A. Ranganatha Mudaliar, Triplicane. Mr. R. S. Desikan of the Presidency College and the Rev. W. B. Harris of the Methodist Mission looked into the manuscript of the work and offered me valuable suggestions for which my thanks are due to them. I must also acknowledge the immense help I received from Dr. M. Varadarajan, Senior Lecturer in Tamil, University of Madras, in going through the proofs. I am indebted to the authorities of the Adyar Library, Adyar especially to Captain G. Srinivasa Murti for undertaking this publication and to Dr. C. Kunhan Raja for his co-operation. I further record my thanks to the Syndicate of the Madras University for permitting me to bring out this publication.

Madras, V. R. R. DIKSHITAR
6th May, 1949

Thirukkural English Translation

by Ramachandra Dikshitar

pāl - iyal -atikāram aṭṭavaṇai

1. aṟattuppāl
1.1 pāyiram / kaṭavuḷ vāḻttu (atikāram 1 - 4)
1.2 illaṟaviyal (atikāram 5 - 24)
1.3 tuṟavaṟaviyal (atikāram 25 - 37)
1.4 ūḻiyal (atikāram 38)

2. poruṭpāl
2.1 araciyal (atikāram 39 - 63)
2.2 amaicciyal (atikāram 64 - 73)
2.3 aṅkaviyal (atikāram 74 - 95)
2.4 oḻipiyal (atikāram 96 - 108)

3. kāmattuppāl
3.1 kaḷaviyal (atikāram 109 - 115)
3.2 kaṟpiyal (atikāram 116 - 133)

I. PREFACE

    1. kaṭavuḷ vāḻttu - CHAPTER 1 — IN PRAISE OF GOD

  1. akaram mutala, eḻuttu ellām; ātipakavaṉ mutaṟṟē, ulaku.

  2. All the letters have the letter ‘A’ as their Origin; this world has God as its origin.

  3. kaṟṟataṉāl āya payaṉ eṉkol-vāl-aṟivaṉ nal tāḷ toḻāar eṉiṉ?.

  4. Of what avail is learning, if the learned do not adore the good feet of Him who is Immaculate Wisdom?

  5. malarmicai ēkiṉāṉ māṇ aṭi cērntār nilamicai nīṭu vāḻvār.

  6. Those who find refuge in the great feet (of Him) who lives in the lotus of the heart (of the devotee) live eternally in heaven.

13 4. vēṇṭutal vēṇṭāmai ilāṉ aṭi cērntārkku yāṇṭum iṭumpai ila.
4. Those who have attained the feet of Him who has no likes or dislikes will be rid of all troubles.

  1. iruḷ cēr iru viṉaiyum cērā, iṟaivaṉ poruḷ cēr pukaḻ purintārmāṭṭu.

  2. Actions, both good and bad that spring from darkness of the mind will never touch those who ever chant the glories of the Lord.

  3. poṟi vāyil aintu avittāṉ poy tīr oḻukka neṟi niṉṟār nīṭu vāḻvār.

  4. Those who still the five senses and walk in truth and right will ever live.

  5. taṉakku uvamai illātāṉ tāḷ cērntārkku allāl, maṉak kavalai māṟṟal aritu.

  6. Only those who have sought refuge in the feet of the peerless can shake off anxiety. Others cannot.

  7. aṟa āḻi antaṇaṉ tāḷ cērntārkku allāl, piṟa āḻi nīntal aritu.

  8. Only those who have clung to the feet of the Lord who is the sea of righteousness, will be able to sail the other seas. Others cannot.

14 9. kōḷ il poṟiyil kuṇam ilavē-eṇkuṇattāṉ tāḷai vaṇaṅkāt talai.
9. The head that does not bow down before and worship the feet of the Lord of the eight attributes, will be as like the palsied senses.

  1. piṟavip peruṅ kaṭal nīntuvar; nīntār, iṟaivaṉ aṭi cērātār.
  2. Those who gain the feet of the Lord cross the great ocean of births; others cannot.

=

    1. vāṉciṟappu -CHAPTER 2 CHAPTER 2 CHAPTER 2 —IN PRAISE OF RAIN IN PRAISE OF RAIN IN PRAISE OF RAIN

  1. vāṉ niṉṟu ulakam vaḻaṅki varutalāṉ, tāṉ amiḻtam eṉṟu uṇaral pāṟṟu.

  2. The world for its existence depends on unfailing rainfall; the rain may well be regarded as the nectar of life.

  3. tuppārkkut tuppu āya tuppu ākki, tuppārkkut tuppu āyatūum maḻai.

  4. The rain is the source of all articles of food that man needs. It becomes his drink too.

  5. viṇ iṉṟu poyppiṉ, virinīr viyaṉ ulakattuuḷ niṉṟu uṭaṟṟum paci. 15

  6. Hunger would stalk abroad and torment this wide sea-girt world were the rims to fail in time.

  7. ēriṉ uḻāar uḻavar, puyal eṉṉum vāri vaḷam kuṉṟikkāl.

  8. The cultivators would cease to plough were the clouds’ free supply of water to fail.

  9. keṭuppatūum, keṭṭārkkuc cārvāy maṟṟu āṅkē eṭuppatūum, ellām maḻai.

  10. It is the rain that afflicts man and it is its fall that relieves him.

  11. vicumpiṉ tuḷi vīḻiṉ allāl, maṟṟu āṅkē pacum pul talai kāṇpu aritu.

  12. If the clouds were to withhold rain not even a blade of grass would rustle on earth.

  13. neṭuṅ kaṭalum taṉ nīrmai kuṉṟum, taṭintu eḻilitāṉ nalkātu ākiviṭiṉ.

  14. Even the illimitable deep shrinks if the clouds do not pour and replenish it.

  15. ciṟappoṭu pūcaṉai cellātu-vāṉam vaṟakkumēl, vāṉōrkkum, īṇṭu. 16

  16. If the rains were to fail there would be no more o£ferings and festivals to the gods.

  17. tāṉam tavam iraṇṭum taṅkā, viyaṉ ulakam vāṉam vaḻaṅkātu eṉiṉ.

  18. If the rains were to fail, there would neither be alms nor penance on this wide earth.

  19. nīr iṉṟu amaiyātu ulakueṉiṉ, yāryārkkum vāṉ iṉṟu amaiyātu oḻukku.

  20. The world cannot exist without water; there will be no ceaseless supply without rainfall.

    1. nīttār perumai - 3. nīttār perumai -CHAPTER 3 CHAPTER 3 CHAPTER 3 —ON THE GREATNESS OF RENUNCIATION ON THE GREATNESS OF RENUNCIATION ON THE GREATNESS OF RENUNCIATION

  1. oḻukkattu nīttār perumai viḻuppattu vēṇṭum- paṉuval tuṇivu.

  2. The one supreme thing all scriptures affirm is the great renunciation of those who walk in right conduct.

  3. tuṟantār perumai tuṇaik kūṟiṉ, vaiyattu iṟantārai eṇṇikkoṇṭaṟṟu.

  4. To measure the greatness of one who has renounced is like reckoning the number of the dead in this world. 17

  5. irumai vakai terintu īṇṭu aṟam pūṇṭār perumai piṟaṅkiṟṟu, ulaku.

  6. The greatest thing on earth is the renunciation of those who understand birth and liberation.

  7. uraṉ eṉṉum tōṭṭiyāṉ, ōr aintum kāppāṉ varaṉ eṉṉum vaippiṟku ōr vittu.

  8. He who with firmness bridles the five senses is (himself) the seed of the eternal bliss. Verily he is the seed of the immortals who with firmness bridles the five senses.

  9. aintu avittāṉ āṟṟal, akal vicumpuḷār kōmāṉ intiraṉē cālum, kari.

  10. Indra, the Lord of the skies is himself a witness, to the might of those who have conquered their five senses.

  11. ceyaṟku ariya ceyvār periyar; ciṟiyar ceyaṟku ariya ceykalātār.

    1. The great achieve the impossible; the little cannot.

  1. cuvai, oḷi, ūṟu, ōcai, nāṟṟam eṉṟu aintiṉ vakai terivāṉkaṭṭē-ulaku. 18

  2. The world falls at the feet of one who has realised the true nature of the taste, sight, touch, sound and smell.

  3. niṟaimoḻi māntar perumai nilattu maṟaimoḻi kāṭṭiviṭum.

  4. The greatness of the sages in this world is borne out by their prophetic utterances.

  5. kuṇam eṉṉum kuṉṟu ēṟi niṉṟār vekuḷi kaṇam ēyum, kāttal aritu.

  6. It is impossible to resist even for a minute the wrath of those who stand on the hill of virtue’s actions.

  7. antaṇar eṉpōr aṟavōr-maṟṟu ev uyirkkum cen taṇmai pūṇṭu oḻukalāṉ.

  8. They are the Brahmans who are righteous and love all creation.

    1. aṟaṉvaliyuṟuttal -CHAPTER 4 CHAPTER 4 CHAPTER 4 —ON DHARMA ON DHARMA ON DHARMA

  1. ciṟappu īṉum; celvamum īṉum; aṟattiṉ ūuṅku ākkam evaṉō, uyirkku.

  2. Is there anything higher in life than Dharma? It secures glory and wealth.

  3. aṟattiṉ ūuṅku ākkamum illai; ataṉai maṟattaliṉ ūṅku illai kēṭu. 19

  4. Nothing is higher than Dharma; to forget it is wrought with greatest evil.

  5. ollum vakaiyāṉ aṟaviṉai ōvātē cellum vāy ellām ceyal.

  6. Avail yourself of all opportunities. Do not cease from practising Dharma on all possible occasions to the best of your ability.

  7. maṉattukkaṇ mācu ilaṉ ātal; aṉaittu aṟaṉ; ākula nīra, piṟa.

  8. Be pure in mind. That is Dharma. All else is but pompous show.

  9. aḻukkāṟu, avā, vekuḷi, iṉṉāc col, nāṉkum iḻukkā iyaṉṟatu-aṟam.

  10. That course of conduct that steers clear of every desire, wrath, and offensive speech — is alone Dharma.

  11. ‘aṉṟu aṟivām’ eṉṉātu, aṟam ceyka; maṟṟu atu poṉṟuṅkāl poṉṟāt tuṇai.

  12. Do not postpone doing Dharma. Do it now. For it will be a never failing friend at your death.

  13. ‘aṟattu āṟu itu’ eṉa vēṇṭā; civikai poṟuttāṉoṭu ūrntāṉ iṭai. 20

    1. Why search for the fruits of Dharma? Behold the one in the palanquin and the

palanquin-bearer.

  1. vīḻ nāḷ paṭāamai naṉṟu āṟṟiṉ, aḵtu oruvaṉ vāḻ nāḷ vaḻi aṭaikkum kal.

  2. If one were to practise righteousness every day it would be the stone that blocks the way to re-birth.

  3. aṟattāṉ varuvatē iṉpam; maṟṟu ellām puṟatta; pukaḻum ila.

  4. Happiness springs only from Dharma. All else is sorrow and merits no praise.

  1. peṇṇiṉ peruntakka yā uḷa-kaṟpu eṉṉum tiṇmai uṇṭākappeṟiṉ?.
    1. Is there anything greater than a woman if only she is the citadel of chastity?

  2. Waking up she worships no other god than her husband. Verily at her very bidding it rains.

24 57. ciṟai kākkum kāppu evaṉ ceyyum? makaḷir niṟai kākkum kāppē talai.

    1. Of what use is one’s watch and ward? Her chastity is her only shield.

  1. peṟṟāṟ peṟiṉ peṟuvar, peṇṭir, peruñ ciṟappup puttēḷir vāḻum ulaku.

  5. ‘maṅkalam’ eṉpa, maṉaimāṭci; maṟṟu ataṉ naṉkalam naṉ makkaṭ pēṟu.

    1. The grace of a home is her virtue. Her blessed children are its adornment.
    1. putalvaraip peṟ 7. putalvaraip peṟutal -CHAPTER 7 CHAPTER 7 CHAPTER 7 —ON SONS ON SONS ON SONS

  1. peṟumavaṟṟuḷ yām aṟivatu illai-aṟivu aṟinta makkaṭpēṟu alla piṟa.

  4. The service a son can do his father is to make the public exclaim ‘see, the fruit of his father’s good deeds.’

    1. aṉpu uṭaimai -CHAPTER 8 CHAPTER 8 CHAPTER 8 —LOVING-KINDNESS KINDNESS KINDNESS

    1. viruntu ōmpal - 9. viruntu ōmpal -Chapter 9 Chapter 9 Chapter 9 —On hospitality On hospitality On hospitality

    1. iṉiyavai kū iyavai kū iyavai kūṟal -CHAPTER 10 CHAPTER 10 CHAPTER 10 —ON SWEET WORDS ON SWEET WORDS ON SWEET WORDS

31

  12. Sweet and inoffensive words yield one happiness both here and hereafter.

    1. ceynnaṉṟ 11. ceynnaṉṟi aṟital -CHAPTER 11 CHAPTER 11 CHAPTER 11—ON GRATITUDE ON GRATITUDE ON GRATITUDE

  19. en naṉṟi koṉṟārkkum uyvu uṇṭām; uyvu illai, ceynnaṉṟi koṉṟa makaṟku.

  20. There is salvation to those guilty of any other sin; but there is no redemption for the sin of ingratitude.

    1. naṭ 12. naṭuvu nilaimai uvu nilaimai uvu nilaimai -CHAPTER 12 CHAPTER 12 CHAPTER 12 —ON EQUITY ON EQUITY ON EQUITY
  1. takuti eṉa oṉṟum naṉṟē-pakutiyāṉ pāṟpaṭṭu oḻukappeṟiṉ.

  14. Not to tilt like the well poised balance is the grace of the wise.

36 119. coṟ kōṭṭam illatu, ceppam-orutalaiyā uṭ kōṭṭam iṉmai peṟiṉ.

  1. vāṇikam ceyvārkku vāṇikam-pēṇip piṟavum tamapōl ceyiṉ.

    1. aṭakkam u akkam u akkam uṭaimai -CHAPTER 13 CHAPTER 13 CHAPTER 13 —ON SELF ON SELF ON SELF-CONTROL CONTROL CONTROL

  1. aṭakkam amararuḷ uykkum; aṭaṅkāmai ār iruḷ uyttuviṭum.

  2. Self-control places one among the gods; lack of it leads one to the darkness of hell.

  3. kākka, poruḷā aṭakkattai-ākkam ataṉiṉ ūṅku illai, uyirkku!.

  4. There is no greater wealth than self-control; treasure it as your wealth.

  6. If one knows the value of self-control and restrains oneself it will bring one fame.

37 124. nilaiyiṉ tiriyātu aṭaṅkiyāṉ tōṟṟam malaiyiṉum māṇap peritu.
124. Loftier than a mountain is the greatness of one who practises self-control.

  1. ellārkkum naṉṟu ām, paṇital; avaruḷḷum celvarkkē celvam takaittu.

  2. Humility becomes all; but it crowns anew the wealthy.

  3. orumaiyuḷ, āmaipōl, aintu aṭakkal āṟṟiṉ, eḻumaiyum ēmāppu uṭaittu.

  5. yā kāvār āyiṉum, nā kākka; kāvākkāl, cōkāppar, col iḻukkup paṭṭu.

  10. The blister caused by fire will heal. But the brand of a bitter tongue will never heal.

  12. The God of righteousness seeks one who is on guard against anger and attains self-control through knowledge.

    1. oḻukkam u ukkam u ukkam uṭaimai -CHAPTER 14 CHAPTER 14 CHAPTER 14 —ON RIGHT CONDUCT ON RIGHT CONDUCT ON RIGHT CONDUCT

  1. oḻukkam viḻuppam taralāṉ, oḻukkam uyiriṉum ōmpappaṭum.

  2. Right conduct exalts one. So it should be prized above one’s life.

  3. parintu ōmpik kākka, oḻukkam-terintu ōmpit tēriṉum, aḵtē tuṇai!.

  4. Strive hard to walk in the right path. One finds in it one’s surest ally.

  5. oḻukkam uṭaimai kuṭimai; iḻukkam iḻinta piṟappāyviṭum.

  6. Right conduct ennobles one’s family. Bad conduct makes one sink in the scale.

  7. maṟappiṉum, ottuk koḷal ākum; pārppāṉ 39 piṟappu oḻukkam kuṉṟak keṭum.

    1. The Brahman may learn anew the Vedas which he forgot. If he were to fall from

his estate he would be lost.

  1. aḻukkāṟu uṭaiyāṉkaṇ ākkam pōṉṟu illaioḻukkam ilāṉkaṇ uyarvu.

  2. The envious do not prosper; likewise one straying from the right path does not advance.

  3. oḻukkattiṉ olkār uravōr-iḻukkattiṉ ētam paṭupākku aṟintu.

  4. The strong of mind will not shrink from virtue; for they know that any deviation is wrought with dire consequences.

  5. oḻukkattiṉ eytuvar, mēṉmai; iḻukkattiṉ eytuvar, eytāp paḻi.

  6. Men of right conduct are crowned with glory. Men of evil ways are covered with disgrace.

  7. naṉṟikku vittu ākum nal oḻukkam; tī oḻukkam eṉṟum iṭumpai tarum.

  8. Good conduct is the spring of happiness. Bad conduct leads one ever to misery.

  9. oḻukkam uṭaiyavarkku ollāvē-tīya 40 vaḻukkiyum, vāyāl colal.

  10. It is difficult for a man of right conduct to utter evil words even in a forgetful mood.

  11. ulakattōṭu oṭṭa oḻukal, pala kaṟṟum, kallār aṟivilātār.

  12. Those who cannot move in harmony with the world are learned fools.

    1. piṟ 15. piṟaṉil viḻaiyāmai aiyāmai aiyāmai -CHAPTER 15 CHAPTER 15 CHAPTER 15 —ON ADULTERY ON ADULTERY ON ADULTERY

  1. piṟaṉ poruḷāḷ-peṭṭu oḻukum pētaimai ñālattu aṟam, poruḷ, kaṇṭārkaṇ il.

  2. The folly of intriguing with another’s wife is not found in one versed in the laws of truth and wealth.

  3. aṟaṉkaṭai niṉṟāruḷ ellām, piṟaṉkaṭai niṉṟāriṉ, pētaiyār il.

  4. Among those who walk in the ways of sin, the most foolish are those who stand at the entrance of another’s (house).

  5. viḷintāriṉ vēṟu allar maṉṟa-teḷintār il tīmai purintu oḻukuvār.

  6. They are as good as dead who misbehave towards the wives of their confiding friends.

41 144. eṉait tuṇaiyar āyiṉum eṉṉām-tiṉait tuṇaiyum tērāṉ, piṟaṉ il pukala?.
144. What avails one’s greatness if one desecrates the sanctity of the house of another reckless of the consequences.

  1. ’eḷitu’ eṉa il iṟappāṉ eytum-eñ ñāṉṟum viḷiyātu niṟkum paḻi.

  2. He who invades (easily) the house of another thinking it a mere trifie will incur eternal infamy.

  3. pakai, pāvam, accam, paḻi eṉa nāṉkum ikavā ām-il iṟappāṉkaṇ.

  4. Four evils, enmity, sin, fear and disgrace dog one who covets another’s wife.

  5. aṟaṉ iyalāṉ ilvāḻvāṉ eṉpāṉ-piṟaṉ iyalāḷ peṇmai nayavātavaṉ.

  6. He is a true householder who does not love another man’s wife.

  7. piṟaṉ maṉai nōkkāta pēr āṇmai, cāṉṟōrkku aṟaṉ oṉṟō?āṉṟa oḻukku.

  8. The heroic manhood that does not lust after another’s wife is to the wise not mere virtue but the very law of their being.

42 149. ’nalakku uriyār yār?’ eṉiṉ, nāma nīr vaippil piṟaṟku uriyāḷ tōḷ tōyātār.
149. Verily he is a gentleman on this sea-girt earth who is free from the sin of adultery.

  1. aṟaṉ varaiyāṉ, alla ceyiṉum, piṟaṉ varaiyāḷ peṇmai nayavāmai naṉṟu.
  2. One may be guilty of any other sins; let one be free from adultery.
    1. poṟ 16. poṟai uṭaimai -CHAPTER 16 CHAPTER 16 CHAPTER 16 —ON PATIE ON PATIE ON PATIENCE

  1. akaḻvārait tāṅkum nilam pōla, tammai ikaḻvārp poṟuttal talai.

  2. The earth sustains even those who dig into her. To bear with those who slander us is the crown of virtue.

  3. poṟuttal, iṟappiṉai eṉṟum; ataṉai maṟattal ataṉiṉum naṉṟu.

  4. Put up always with one’s transgressions. Far greater than one’s forbearance is one’s oblivion of them.

  5. iṉmaiyuḷ iṉmai viruntu orāl; vaṉmaiyuḷ vaṉmai maṭavārp poṟai.

  6. Poverty within poverty is denying hospitality to guests; grace within grace is bearing with the foolish. 43

  7. niṟai uṭaimai nīṅkāmai vēṇṭiṉ, poṟai uṭaimai pōṟṟi oḻukappaṭum.

    1. If one wishes to maintain character one’s conduct must be marked by patience.

  1. oṟuttārai oṉṟāka vaiyārē; vaippar, poṟuttāraip poṉpōl potintu.

  2. The world takes no note of the avenger but it esteems the patient like gold.

  3. oṟuttārkku oru nāḷai iṉpam; poṟuttārkkup poṉṟum tuṇaiyum pukaḻ.

  4. The delight of the avenger is for a day. The joy of the forbearing lasts till the end of the earth.

  5. tiṟaṉ alla taṉ-piṟar ceyyiṉum, nō nontu, aṟaṉ alla ceyyāmai naṉṟu.

  6. Resist not a wrong however grievous but forgive out of pity other’s transgressions.

  7. mikutiyāṉ mikkavai ceytārait tām tam takutiyāṉ veṉṟuviṭal!.

  8. Conquer with forbearance one who has done you harm in one’s insolent pride.

44 159. tuṟantāriṉ tūymai uṭaiyar-iṟantārvāy iṉṉāc col nōṟkiṟpavar.
159. Greater than an ascetic is one who endures the insolent words of the transgressor.

  1. uṇṇātu nōṟpār periyar-piṟar collum iṉṉāc col nōṟpāriṉ piṉ.
  2. Great are those who fast and do penance but greater than they are those who put up with insults.
    1. aḻukkāṟāmai -CHAPTER 17 CHAPTER 17 CHAPTER 17 —ON ENVY ON ENVY ON ENVY

  1. oḻukku āṟāk koḷka-oruvaṉ taṉ neñcattu aḻukkāṟu ilāta iyalpu.

  2. Let no one have envy; for freedom from envy must be one’s virtue.

  3. viḻup pēṟṟiṉ aḵtu oppatu illai-yārmāṭṭum aḻukkāṟṟiṉ aṉmai peṟiṉ.

  4. Envy none; there is no other possession greater than one’s freedom from it.

  5. aṟaṉ, ākkam, vēṇṭātāṉ eṉpāṉ piṟaṉ ākkam pēṇātu aḻukkaṟuppāṉ.

    1. He who envies other’s riches neither loves virtue nor wealth.

45 164. aḻukkāṟṟiṉ allavai ceyyār-iḻukku āṟṟiṉ ētam paṭupākku aṟintu.
164. The wise do not commit any wrong out of envy; for, they know the evils that spring from it.

  1. aḻukkāṟu uṭaiyārkku atu cālum- oṉṉār vaḻukkiyum kēṭu īṉpatu.

  2. The envious need no enemies to work their own ruin; for they find in their envy their sufficient foe.

  3. koṭuppatu aḻukkaṟuppāṉ cuṟṟam uṭuppatūum uṇpatūum iṉṟik keṭum.

    1. The envious that stand in the way of charity perish with their kith and kin.

  1. avvittu aḻukkāṟu uṭaiyāṉaic ceyyavaḷ tavvaiyaik kāṭṭi viṭum.

  2. Fortune forsakes the envious to her elder sister.

  3. aḻukkāṟu eṉa oru pāvi tiruc ceṟṟu, tīyuḻi uyttuviṭum.

  4. Envy is a deadly sin. It blights one’s fortune and casts one into hell.

  5. avviya neñcattāṉ ākkamum, cevviyāṉ kēṭum, niṉaikkappaṭum. 46

  6. The prosperity of the envious and the adversity of the virtuous afford food for reflection.

  7. aḻukkaṟṟu akaṉṟārum illai; aḵtu illār perukkattiṉ tīrntārum il.

  8. Envy never thrives; fortune never forsakes one who is free from it.

    1. veḵ 18. veḵkāmai -CHAPTER 18 CHAPTER 18 CHAPTER 18 —ON NON-COVETING COVETING COVETING

  1. naṭuvu iṉṟi naṉ poruḷ veḵkiṉ, kuṭi poṉṟi, kuṟṟamum āṅkē tarum.

  2. Iniquitous coveting of wealth results in the ruin of one’s home and brings in its train many sins.

  3. paṭu payaṉ veḵki, paḻippaṭuva ceyyārnaṭuvu aṉmai nāṇupavar.

  4. Those who stand for equity do not commit sinful acts through covetousness.

  5. ciṟṟiṉpam veḵki, aṟaṉ alla ceyyārēmaṟṟu iṉpam vēṇṭupavar.

  6. Those who seek eternal happiness will never commit unrighteous acts through love of low pleasures.

  7. ‘ilam’ eṉṟu veḵkutal ceyyār-pulam veṉṟa 47 puṉmai il kāṭciyavar.

  8. The spotless wise who have conquered their senses though destitute, will not covet other’s wealth.

  9. aḵki akaṉṟa aṟivu eṉ ām-yārmāṭṭum veḵki, veṟiya ceyiṉ?.

  10. Of what avail is one’s keen and penetrating intellect if one through covetousness acts foolishly?

  11. aruḷ veḵki, āṟṟiṉkaṇ niṉṟāṉ, poruḷ veḵkip pollāta cūḻa, keṭum.

  12. Even he who treads the path of grace comes to ruin through covetous intentions.

  13. vēṇṭaṟka, veḵki ām ākkam-viḷaivayiṉ māṇṭaṟku aritu ām payaṉ!.

  14. Covet not other’s wealth for out of covetousness spring evils.

  15. ‘aḵkāmai celvattiṟku yātu?’ eṉiṉ, veḵkāmai vēṇṭum piṟaṉ kaip poruḷ.

  16. Preservation of one’s property lies through one’s freedom from covetousness.

  17. aṟaṉ aṟintu veḵkā aṟivu uṭaiyārc cērumtiṟaṉ aṟintu āṅkē tiru. 48

  18. The wise who know what is righteous covet not; the Goddess of Fortune would seek them unbidden.

  19. iṟal īṉum, eṇṇātu veḵkiṉ; viṟal īṉum, vēṇṭāmai eṉṉum cerukku.

  20. A blind covetousness brings about one’s ruin. Freedom from it begets one’s triumph.

    1. puṟ 19. puṟam kūṟāmai -CHAPTER 19 CHAPTER 19 CHAPTER 19 —ON NOT BACK ON NOT BACK ON NOT BACK-BITING

  1. aṟam kūṟāṉ, alla ceyiṉum, oruvaṉ puṟam kūṟāṉ eṉṟal iṉitu.

  2. One may be guilty of wrongful deeds, but let not one be guilty of slander.

  3. aṟaṉ aḻīi allavai ceytaliṉ tītēpuṟaṉ aḻīip poyttu nakai.

  4. More heinous than sin is the deceitful smile of a slanderer.

  5. puṟam kūṟi, poyttu, uyir vāḻtaliṉ, cātal aṟam kūṟum ākkam tarum.

  6. Prefer death to a life of slander; for one finds in it the fruit of one’s virtue.

  7. kaṇ niṉṟu, kaṇ aṟac colliṉum, collaṟkamuṉ iṉṟu piṉ nōkkāc col. 49

  8. Talk your bitterest to one’s face but abstain from wanton slander.

  9. aṟam collum neñcattāṉ aṉmai puṟam collum puṉmaiyāl kāṇappaṭum.

  10. The tongue of the base slanderer that talks of virtue belies his heart.

  11. piṟaṉ paḻi kūṟuvāṉ taṉ paḻiyuḷḷum tiṟaṉ terintu kūṟappaṭum.

  12. Ye scandal-mongers, beware of your being scandalized.

  13. pakac collik kēḷirp pirippar-nakac colli naṭpu āṭal tēṟṟātavar.

  14. Those who alienate friends by back-biting may have forgotten the art of making friends through suavity of speech.

  15. tuṉṉiyār kuṟṟamum tūṟṟum marapiṉār, eṉṉaikol, ētilārmāṭṭu?.

  16. Those who trumpet the faults of their closest friends, what would they not do in the case of strangers?

  17. aṟaṉ nōkki āṟṟum kol vaiyam-puṟaṉ nōkkip puṉ col uraippāṉ poṟai.

  18. How the earth bears the heavy burden of one who scandalises others! Perhaps patience is her virtue. 50

  19. ētilār kuṟṟampōl tam kuṟṟam kāṇkiṟpiṉ, tītu uṇṭō, maṉṉum uyirakku?.

  20. Will ever harm befall one who looks upon the faults of others as one’s own?

    1. payaṉ 20. payaṉila collāmai ila collāmai ila collāmai -CHAPTER 20 CHAPTER 20 CHAPTER 20 —ON FRIVOLITY OF SPEECH ON FRIVOLITY OF SPEECH ON FRIVOLITY OF SPEECH

  1. pallār muṉiyap payaṉ ila colluvāṉ ellārum eḷḷappaṭum.

  2. He who revels in frivolous talk will be despised by all.

  3. payaṉ ila pallārmuṉ collal, nayaṉ ila naṭṭārkaṇ ceytaliṉ tītu.

  4. To talk frivolously in the presence of many is worse than an unjust act towards friends.

  5. nayaṉ ilaṉ eṉpatu collum-payaṉ ila pārittu uraikkum urai.

  6. Indulgence in useless words at once betrays one’s lack of probity.

  7. nayaṉ cārā naṉmaiyiṉ nīkkum-payaṉ cārāp paṇpu il col pallārakattu.

  8. Uttering empty words before all deprives one of one’s sense of justice and mars one’s noble qualities. 51

  9. cīrmai ciṟappoṭu nīṅkum-payaṉ ila nīrmai uṭaiyār coliṉ.

  10. If good-natured men speak profitless words, their greatness and glory will disappear.

  11. payaṉ il col pārāṭṭuvāṉai makaṉ eṉal! makkaṭ pataṭi eṉal!.

    1. He is not a man but the chaff among men, who indulges in vain words.

  1. nayaṉ ila colliṉum colluka! cāṉṟōr payaṉ ila collāmai naṉṟu.

  2. Let great men speak untruth; it is better they refrain from uttering useless words.

  3. arum payaṉ āyum aṟiviṉār collārperum payaṉ illāta col.

  4. Men of great discernment will never speak words devoid of great import.

  5. poruḷ tīrnta poccāntum collār-maruḷ tīrnta mācu aṟu kāṭciyavar.

  6. Men of unclouded wisdom never utter nonsense even in a forgetful mood.

  7. colluka, collil payaṉ uṭaiya! collaṟka, 52 collil payaṉ ilāc col!.

  8. Speak profitable words; avoid nonsense.

    1. tīviṉ 21. tīviṉai accam ai accam ai accam -CHAPTER 21 CHAPTER 21 CHAPTER 21 —ON FEAR OF EVIL DEEDS ON FEAR OF EVIL DEEDS ON FEAR OF EVIL DEEDS

  1. tīviṉaiyār añcār; viḻumiyār añcuvartīviṉai eṉṉum cerukku.

  2. Men hardened in sins do not fear evil; but the good dread it.

  3. tīyavai tīya payattalāṉ, tīyavai tīyiṉum añcappaṭum.

  4. Evil is to be dreaded more than fire; for it lands one in disaster.

  5. aṟiviṉuḷ ellām talai eṉpa-tīya ceṟuvārkkum ceyyā viṭal.

  6. Not to return evil to those who do evil unto you, is, they say, the crown of wisdom.

  7. maṟantum piṟaṉ kēṭu cūḻaṟka! cūḻiṉ, aṟam cūḻum, cūḻntavaṉ kēṭu.

  8. Let none plot evil to others even in forgetfulness. If he does so, the God of Righteousness will compass his ruin.

  9. ‘ilaṉ’ eṉṟu tīyavai ceyyaṟka! ceyyiṉ, 53 ilaṉ ākum, maṟṟum peyarttu.

  10. Let none do wrong on account of poverty; if he does so he becomes poorer still.

  11. tīp pāla tāṉ piṟarkaṇ ceyyaṟka-nōyp pāla taṉṉai aṭal vēṇṭātāṉ!.

  12. Let not one do evil unto others, if one wants to be free from affliction.

  13. eṉaip pakai uṟṟārum uyvar; viṉaip pakai vīyātu, piṉ ceṉṟu, aṭum.

  14. You may escape your enemies but your evil follows you and hunts you down relentlessly.

  15. tīyavai ceytār keṭutal niḻal taṉṉai vīyātu aṭi uṟaintaṟṟu.

  16. Evil dogs you close on your heels like a shadow.

  17. taṉṉait tāṉ kātalaṉ āyiṉ, eṉaittu oṉṟum tuṉṉaṟka, tīviṉaip pāl!.

  18. If one really loves oneself let one not do any harm to others.

  19. aruṅ kēṭaṉ eṉpatu aṟika-maruṅku ōṭit tīviṉai ceyyāṉ eṉiṉ?.

  20. Hardly doth sorrow befall one who does not deviate from right.

54

    1. oppuravu aṟ 22. oppuravu aṟital -CHAPTER 22 CHAPTER 22 CHAPTER 22 —ON DECORUM ON DECORUM ON DECORUM

  1. kaimmāṟu vēṇṭā kaṭappāṭu; mārimāṭṭu eṉ āṟṟum kollō, ulaku?.

  2. Do not expect any return for the services (duty) done. What does the world give in exchange for the clouds that pour rain?

  3. tāḷ āṟṟit tanta poruḷ ellām takkārkku vēḷāṇmai ceytaṟporuṭṭu.

  4. All the wealth one earns is for rendering help to the deserving.

  5. puttēḷ ulakattum, īṇṭum, peṟal aritēoppuraviṉ nalla piṟa.

  6. Is there anything greater than decorum either here or in the world to come?

  7. ottatu aṟivāṉ uyir vāḻvāṉ; maṟṟaiyāṉ cettāruḷ vaikkappaṭum.

  8. Verily he is alive who is in harmony with the world; others should be ranked with the dead.

  9. ūruṇi nīr niṟaintaṟṟē-ulaku avām pēr aṟivāḷaṉ tiru.

  10. The wealth of the wise is a never-failing spring.

55 216. payaṉ maram uḷḷūrp paḻuttaṟṟāl-celvam nayaṉ uṭaiyāṉkaṇ paṭiṉ.
216. The wealth of the truly liberal is like a tree ripening in the heart of a village.

  1. maruntu ākit tappā marattaṟṟāl-celvam peruntakaiyāṉkaṇ paṭiṉ.

  2. The wealth of the generous is like a healing medicinal tree.

  3. iṭaṉ il paruvattum, oppuraviṟku olkārkaṭaṉ aṟi kāṭciyavar.

  4. Even in poverty the truly discerning never ceases to be liberal.

  5. nayaṉ uṭaiyāṉ nalkūrntāṉ ātal ceyum nīra ceyyātu amaikalā āṟu.

  6. The poverty of the liberal of heart is his failure in the offices of tenderness.

  7. ‘oppuraviṉāl varum, kēṭu’ eṉiṉ, aḵtu oruvaṉ viṟṟuk kōḷ takkatu uṭaittu.

    1. The poverty that results from a just course of action is worth purchasing by

going into the very bond of slavery.

56

    1. īkai - 23. īkai -CHAPTER 23 CHAPTER 23 CHAPTER 23—ON LIBERALITY ON LIBERALITY ON LIBERALITY
  1. vaṟiyārkku oṉṟu īvatē īkai; maṟṟu ellām kuṟiyetirppai nīratu uṭaittu.
    1. Gift to the poor alone is true charity. Everything else is of the nature of a barter.

  1. ’nallāṟu’ eṉiṉum, koḷal tītu; ‘mēl ulakam il’ eṉiṉum, ītalē naṉṟu.

  2. Receiving gifts is bad though one is assured of heaven. Bestowing gifts is good, though thereby one should be bereft of it.

  3. ‘ilaṉ’ eṉṉum evvam uraiyāmai ītal kulaṉ uṭaiyāṉkaṇṇē uḷa.

    1. The innately noble never beg but give ere charity begins.
  1. iṉṉātu, irakkappaṭutal-irantavar iṉ mukam kāṇum aḷavu.
    1. Even to be begged is miserable for we feel wretched till the beggar’s face is lit

with joy.

  1. āṟṟuvār āṟṟal paci āṟṟal; ap paciyai māṟṟuvār āṟṟaliṉ piṉ.

  2. Endurance of one’s hunger is the test of one’s penance. Far greater than that endurance is the spirit of appeasing the hunger of others. 57

  3. aṟṟār aḻi paci tīrttal! aḵtu oruvaṉ peṟṟāṉ poruḷ vaippu uḻi.

    1. Let the rich appease the devouring hunger of the indigent poor. It is a charity

rendered unto themselves.

  1. pāttu ūṇ marīiyavaṉaip paci eṉṉum tīp piṇi tīṇṭal aritu.
    1. The pest of hunger never touches one who shares one’s food with the poor.
  1. īttu uvakkum iṉpam aṟiyārkol-tām uṭaimai vaittu iḻakkum vaṉ kaṇavar?.
    1. The callous rich hide their barren metal; perhaps they know not the joy of giving.

  1. irattaliṉ iṉṉātu maṉṟa-nirappiya tāmē tamiyar uṇal.

  2. More squalid than begging is a life of self-indulgence.

  3. cātaliṉ iṉṉātatu illai; iṉitu, atūum ītal iyaiyākkaṭai.

  4. Death indeed is the greatest calamity; worse than death is one’s failure in charity.

58

    1. pukaḻ 24. pukaḻ-CHAPTER 24 CHAPTER 24 CHAPTER 24 -ON RENOWN ON RENOWN ON RENOWN
  1. ītal! icaipaṭa vāḻtal! atu allatu ūtiyam illai, uyirkku.
    1. Give and make a name. There is no greater gain to man than such a renown.
  1. uraippār uraippavai ellām irappārkku oṉṟu īvārmēl niṟkum pukaḻ.
    1. The one undying theme of praise is the praise of charity.

  1. oṉṟā ulakattu uyarnta pukaḻ allāl, poṉṟātu niṟpatu oṉṟu il.

  2. Nothing lasts save one’s fearless renown.

  3. nila varai nīḷ pukaḻ āṟṟiṉ, pulavaraip pōṟṟātu, puttēḷ ulaku.

  4. The wise are not favoured of the gods; but the’ renowned on earth are adored by them.

  5. nattampōl kēṭum, uḷatākum cākkāṭum, vittakarkku allāl aritu.

  6. Out of death and ruin the wise fashion things enduring.

  7. tōṉṟiṉ, pukaḻoṭu tōṉṟuka! aḵtu ilār 59 tōṉṟaliṉ tōṉṟāmai naṉṟu.

    1. Let man be born to achieve renown. Let not the unrenowned see the light of

day.

  1. pukaḻpaṭa vāḻātār tam nōvār, tammai ikaḻvārai nōvatu evaṉ?.
    1. Let the inglorious blame themselves. Let them not reproach others.
  1. ‘vacai’ eṉpa, vaiyattārkku ellām-’icai’ eṉṉum eccam peṟāaviṭiṉ.
    1. World’s reproach befalls one who does not achieve lasting fame.
  1. vacai ilā vaṇ payaṉ kuṉṟum-icai ilā yākkai poṟutta nilam.
    1. In a land which bears the burden of the unrenowned even nature’s bounty is on

the wane.

  1. vacai oḻiya vāḻvārē vāḻvār; icai oḻiya vāḻvārē vāḻātavar.
  2. The unblemished truly live; the unrenowned merely exist.

End of the Section on Domestic Life

60 1.3. tuṟ 1.3. tuṟavaṟaviyal -III. ON RENUNCIATION III. ON RENUNCIATION III. ON RENUNCIATION

    1. aruḷ 25. aruḷuṭaimai -CHAPTER 25 CHAPTER 25 CHAPTER 25 —ON COMPASSION ON COMPASSION ON COMPASSION

  1. aruṭ celvam, celvattuḷ celvam; poruṭ celvam pūriyārkaṇṇum uḷa.

  2. The crown of wealth is one’s compassion; all other wealth is found even among meanest of men.

  3. nal āṟṟāṉ nāṭi aruḷ āḷka! pal āṟṟāṉ tēriṉum aḵtē tuṇai.

  4. Be compassionate; for compassion is the pivot of all tenets.

  5. aruḷ cērnta neñciṉārkku illai-iruḷ cērnta iṉṉā ulakam pukal.

  6. The compassionate know not hell.

  7. ‘maṉ uyir ōmpi, aruḷ āḷvāṟku il’ eṉpa- ‘taṉ uyir añcum viṉai’.

  8. Freedom from dread of sin is only for the compassionate that love all creation.

  9. allal, aruḷ āḷvārkku illai; vaḷi vaḻaṅkum mallal mā ñālam kari.

  10. The compassionate know not life’s agonies; verily the wind-blown earth is witness to it.

61 246. ‘poruḷ nīṅkip poccāntār’ eṉpar-‘aruḷ nīṅki allavai ceytu oḻukuvār’.
246. The cruel that delight in sin perhaps know not what awaits them.

  1. aruḷ illārkku av ulakam illai-poruḷ illārkku iv ulakam illākiyāṅku.

  2. Heaven is not for the unfeeling; earth is not for the indigent.

  3. poruḷ aṟṟār pūppar orukāl; aruḷ aṟṟār aṟṟār; maṟṟu ātal aritu.

  4. Fortune may smile on the ruined; the un feeling are the unredeemed.

  5. teruḷātāṉ meypporuḷ kaṇṭaṟṟāl-tēriṉ, aruḷātāṉ ceyyum aṟam.

  6. Behold the unfeeling seeking virtue; it is like ignorance seeing light.

  7. valiyār muṉ taṉṉai niṉaikka-tāṉ taṉṉiṉ meliyārmēl cellum iṭattu.

  8. Oppress not the weak; remember your fate in stronger hands.

    1. pulāl maṟ 26. pulāl maṟuttal -CHAPTER 26 CHAPTER 26 CHAPTER 26 —ON ABSTAINING FROM MEAT ON ABSTAINING FROM MEAT ON ABSTAINING FROM MEAT

  1. taṉ ūṉ perukkaṟkut tāṉ piṟitu ūṉ uṇpāṉ eṅṅaṉam āḷum aruḷ?. 62

  2. He who fattens on the flesh of animals, can he ever understand the rule of love?

  3. poruḷ āṭci pōṟṟātārkku illai; aruḷ āṭci āṅku illai, ūṉ tiṉpavarkku.

  4. Wealth is not for the unwary. Compassion is not for the flesh-eater.

  5. paṭai koṇṭār neñcam pōl naṉṟu ūkkātu-oṉṟaṉ uṭal cuvai uṇṭār maṉam.

  6. The heart of a flesh-eater is devoid of love like that of the wielder of a deadly weapon.

  7. ‘aruḷ’, allatu, yātu?’ eṉiṉ,-kollāmai, kōṟal: poruḷ allatu, av ūṉ tiṉal.

  8. What is compassion but refraining from killing; what is sin but eating flesh?

  9. uṇṇāmai uḷḷatu uyirnilai; ūṉ uṇṇa, aṇṇāttal ceyyātu, aḷaṟu.

  10. Will there be throb of life when there is flesh-eating? Will there be any escape from hell for the flesh-eater?

  11. tiṉaṟporuṭṭāl kollātu ulaku eṉiṉ, yārum vilaip poruṭṭāl ūṉ taruvār il.

  12. Would there be meat for sale, if men were not to kill animals for eating flesh?

63 257. uṇṇāmai vēṇṭum, pulāal-piṟitu oṉṟaṉ puṇ; atu uṇarvārp peṟiṉ.
257. If one realises that meat is nothing but the wound of another creature, one refrains from eating it.

  1. ceyiriṉ talaip pirinta kāṭciyār uṇṇār, uyiriṉ talaippirinta ūṉ.

  2. Men of clear vision abstain from the flesh of a slaughtered animal.

  3. avi corintu āyiram vēṭṭaliṉ, oṉṟaṉ uyir cekuttu uṇṇāmai naṉṟu.

  4. Far nobler than a thousand oblations on fire is an act of abstinence from flesh.

  5. kollāṉ, pulālai maṟuttāṉaik kaikūppi, ellā uyirum toḻum.

  6. The whole world folds its hands in prayer to one who kills not and abjures flesh.

    1. tavam - 27. tavam -CHAPTER 27 CHAPTER 27 CHAPTER 27 —ON PENANCE ON PENANCE ON PENANCE
  1. uṟṟa nōy nōṉṟal, uyirkku uṟukaṇ ceyyāmai, aṟṟē-tavattiṟku uru.
  2. The true form of penance is to put up with all pain and to abstain from injury.

64 262. tavamum tavam uṭaiyārkku ākum; avam, ataṉai aḵtu ilār mēṟkoḷvatu.
262. Penance is possible only for the disciplined. Disgrace attends the undisciplined.

  1. tuṟantārkkut tuppuravu vēṇṭi, maṟantārkolmaṟṟaiyavarkaḷ, tavam!.

  2. In their ministering to the needs of the ascetic, verily the householders have become oblivious of their penance.

  3. oṉṉārt teṟalum, uvantārai ākkalum, eṇṇiṉ, tavattāṉ varum.

  4. Penance, if it wills can mar its foe, or bless its friend.

  5. vēṇṭiya vēṇṭiyāṅku eytalāṉ, cey tavam īṇṭu muyalappaṭum.

    1. They persevere in penance; for through penance they achieve their desired

goal.

  1. tavam ceyvār tam karumam ceyvār; maṟṟu allār avam ceyvār, ācaiyuḷ paṭṭu.

  2. To do penance is to be alive to one’s duty; those enmeshed in desire come to ruin.

  3. cuṭac cuṭarum poṉpōl oḷiviṭum-tuṉpam 65 cuṭaccuṭa nōṟkiṟpavarkku.

  4. Gold shines all the more in fire; those who do penance become mellowed through suffering.

  5. taṉ uyir tāṉ aṟap peṟṟāṉai ēṉaiya maṉ uyir ellām toḻum.

  6. The world worships one who has regained one’s soul.

  7. kūṟṟam kutittalum kaikūṭum-nōṟṟaliṉ āṟṟal talaippaṭṭavarkku.

  8. Men at the height of their penance can triumph over even death.

  9. ilar palar ākiya kāraṇam-nōṟpār cilar; palar nōlātavar.

  10. Many are the indigent; for only a few practise penance.

    1. kūṭ 28. kūṭā oḻukkam -CHAPTER 28 CHAPTER 28 CHAPTER 28—ON IMPROPER CONDUCT ON IMPROPER CONDUCT ON IMPROPER CONDUCT

  1. vañca maṉattāṉ paṭiṟṟu oḻukkam pūtaṅkaḷ aintum akattē nakum.

  2. A man’s five senses will laugh within at the false conduct of a deceitful mind.

  3. vāṉ uyar tōṟṟam evaṉ ceyyum-taṉ neñcam tāṉ aṟi kuṟṟapaṭiṉ?. 66

  4. Of what avail is a man’s saintly mien, if his mind is bent on evil?

  5. vali il nilaimaiyāṉ val uruvam peṟṟam puliyiṉ tōl pōrttu mēyntaṟṟu.

  6. The ascetic appearance of one who has no strength of will, is like that of an ox grazing in the guise of a tiger.

  7. tavam maṟaintu, allavai ceytal-putalmaṟaintu vēṭṭuvaṉ puḷ cimiḻttaṟṟu.

  8. Committing evil under the mask of holiness is like the hunter lying in wait for birds.

  9. ‘paṟṟu aṟṟēm’ eṉpār paṭiṟṟu oḻukkam. ‘eṟṟu! eṟṟu!’ eṉṟu ētam palavum tarum.

  10. The hypocrisy of one who professes asceticism lands one in endless troubles.

  11. neñciṉ tuṟavār, tuṟantārpōl vañcittu, vāḻvāriṉ vaṉkaṇār il.

  12. There is none so hardened in vice as one who though hollow at heart, wears the mask of saintliness.

  13. puṟam kuṉṟi kaṇṭaṉaiyarēṉum, akam kuṉṟi mūkkil kariyār uṭaittu. 67

  14. This world contains (many) men who like the Kunri seed are fair of face but foul of heart.

  15. maṉattatu mācu āka, māṇṭār nīr āṭi, maṟaintu oḻukum māntar palar.

  16. There are many insincere men who frequent sacred waters to pass for holy men.

  17. kaṇai koṭitu; yāḻ kōṭu cevvitu; āṅku aṉṉa viṉaipaṭu pālāl koḷal.

  18. The arrow, though straight is deadly; the yāl though crooked is sweet. Let people be judged by their actions.

  19. maḻittalum nīṭṭalum vēṇṭā- ulakam paḻittatu oḻittuviṭiṉ.

  20. If persons abstain from deeds condemned by the world there is no need either for tonsure or for matted locks.

    1. kaḷḷ 29. kaḷḷāmai -CHAPTER 29 CHAPTER 29 CHAPTER 29—ON NON-STEALING STEALING STEALING
  1. eḷḷāmai vēṇṭuvāṉ eṉpāṉ eṉaittu oṉṟum kaḷḷāmai kākka, taṉ neñcu!.
  2. He who wants to command respect must guard his mind against robbing others.

68 282. uḷḷattāl uḷḷalum tītē; ‘piṟaṉ poruḷaik kaḷḷattāl kaḷvēm’ eṉal!.
282. It is a sin to lust for another’s belongings.

  1. kaḷaviṉāl ākiya ākkam, aḷavu iṟantu, āvatu pōla, keṭum.

  2. Ill-gotten wealth however vast comes to nought.

  3. kaḷaviṉkaṇ kaṉṟiya kātal viḷaiviṉkaṇ vīyā viḻumam tarum.

  4. Inordinate desire to steal brings in its train endless suffering.

  5. aruḷ karuti aṉpuṭaiyar ātal poruḷ karutip poccāppup pārppārkaṇ il.

  6. Can ever grace and love be found in one who exploits the unwary?

  7. aḷaviṉkaṇ niṉṟu oḻukalāṟṟār-kaḷaviṉkaṇ kaṉṟiya kātalavar.

  8. Those who have a burning desire to steal cannot walk in the path of virtue.

  9. kaḷavu eṉṉum kār aṟivu āṇmai aḷavu eṉṉum āṟṟal purintārkaṇ il.

  10. The dark thought of stealing is absent in those who are alive to the value of life.

69 288. aḷavu aṟintār neñcattu aṟampōla, niṟkum, kaḷavu aṟintār neñcil karavu.
288. Virtue dwells in the person of known probity; deceit dwells in persons addicted to stealing.

  1. aḷavu alla ceytu, āṅkē vīvar-kaḷavu alla maṟṟaiya tēṟṟātavar.

  2. Those who know nothing else than stealing will indulge in unrighteous acts and forthwith perish.

  3. kaḷvārkkut taḷḷum, uyirnilai; kaḷḷārkkut taḷḷātu, puttēḷ ulaku.

  4. Their very bodies fail the defrauding. The world of the gods fail not the upright.

    1. vāymai - 30. vāymai -CHAPTER 30 CHAPTER 30 CHAPTER 30—ON TRUTH ON TRUTH ON TRUTH

  1. ‘vāymai eṉappaṭuvatu yātu?’ eṉiṉ, yātu oṉṟum tīmai ilāta colal.

  2. What is truth but unsullied utterance?

  3. poymmaiyum vāymai iṭatta-purai tīrnta naṉmai payakkum eṉiṉ.

  4. Even untruth has the stamp of truth, if it is free from harm.

70 293. taṉ neñcu aṟivatu poyyaṟka; poyttapiṉ, taṉ neñcē taṉṉaic cuṭum.
293. Let none utter a falsehood against his conscience lest it should torment him.

  1. uḷḷattāl poyyātu oḻukiṉ, ulakattār uḷḷattuḷ ellām uḷaṉ.

  2. One sits high in the hearts of all who is true to oneself.

  3. maṉattoṭu vāymai moḻiyiṉ, tavattoṭu tāṉam ceyvāriṉ talai.

  4. Far greater than a benefactor or an ascetic is one whose words come from the depths of truth.

  5. poyyāmai aṉṉa pukaḻ illai; eyyāmai, ellā aṟamum tarum.

  6. One’s renown is rooted only in truth; it leads one easily to every other virtue.

  7. poyyāmai poyyāmai āṟṟiṉ, aṟam piṟa ceyyāmai ceyyāmai naṉṟu.

  8. Practise truth, you need not practise any other virtue.

  9. puṟam tūymai nīrāl amaiyum;- akam tūymai vāymaiyāl kāṇappaṭum. 71

  10. Water cleanses the body; truth cleanses the soul.

  11. ellā viḷakkum viḷakku alla; cāṉṟōrkkup poyyā viḷakkē viḷakku.

  12. All lamps are not lamps. To the great the lamp of truth is the lamp.

  13. yām meyyāk kaṇṭavaṟṟuḷ, illai-eṉaittu oṉṟum vāymaiyiṉ nalla piṟa.

  14. In all the scriptures we have read, there is no virtue greater than truth.

    1. vekuḷ 31. vekuḷāmai -CHAPTER 31 CHAPTER 31 CHAPTER 31—ON NOT GETTING ANGRY ON NOT GETTING ANGRY ON NOT GETTING ANGRY

  1. cel iṭattuk kāppāṉ ciṉam kāppāṉ; al iṭattu, kākkiṉ eṉ? kāvākkāl eṉ?.

  2. He who restrains his wrath where it can be vented shows real restraint. What does it matter whether one restrains it or not in an unavailing hour?

  3. cellā iṭattuc ciṉam tītu; cel iṭattum, il, ataṉiṉ tīya piṟa.

  4. Anger is bad even where it is unavailing; but where it can be effectively exercised there is no worse evil.

  5. maṟattal, vekuḷiyai yārmāṭṭum-tīya piṟattal ataṉāṉ varum. 72

  6. Do not get angry with any one; for out of anger springs forth a host of evils.

  7. nakaiyum uvakaiyum kollum ciṉattiṉ pakaiyum uḷavō, piṟa?.

  8. Is there any enemy other than anger that kills both joy and pleasure?

  9. taṉṉait tāṉ kākkiṉ, ciṉam kākka! kāvākkāl, taṉṉaiyē kollum, ciṉam.

  10. If a man were to guard himself let him restrain anger. Otherwise anger gets the better of him.

  11. ciṉam eṉṉum cērntāraikkolli iṉam eṉṉum ēmap puṇaiyaic cuṭum.

  12. Anger destroys even one’s kindred who is the canoe of his life.

  13. ciṉattaip poruḷ eṉṟu koṇṭavaṉ kēṭu nilattu aṟaintāṉ kai piḻaiyātaṟṟu.

  14. The ruin of one who nourishes wrath is as certain as the injury to one’s hands when beat on the ground.

  15. iṇar eri tōyvaṉṉa iṉṉā ceyiṉum, puṇariṉ vekuḷāmai naṉṟu.

  16. It is better you show no wrath even against one who inflicts on you harm scorching you like a thousand-tongued flame. 73

  17. uḷḷiya ellām uṭaṉ eytum-uḷḷattāl uḷḷāṉ vekuḷi eṉiṉ.

  18. Banish anger from your mind; you get all that you long for.

  19. iṟantār iṟantār aṉaiyar; ciṉattait tuṟantār tuṟantār tuṇai.

  20. Men given to wrath are one with the devil; Men free from it are one with the immortals.

    1. iṉṉ 32. iṉṉā ceyyāmai ā ceyyāmai ā ceyyāmai -CHAPTER 32 CHAPTER 32 CHAPTER 32—ON NOT DOING EVIL ON NOT DOING EVIL ON NOT DOING EVIL

  1. ciṟappu īṉum celvam peṟiṉum, piṟarkku iṉṉā ceyyāmai mācu aṟṟār kōḷ.

  2. It is the nature of the spotless not to inflict suffering on others, though by it they may get wealth and renown.

  3. kaṟuttu iṉṉā ceyta akkaṇṇum, maṟuttu iṉṉā ceyyāmai mācu aṟṟār kōḷ.

  4. It is the nature of the stainless not to resist evil.

  5. ceyyāmal ceṟṟārkkum iṉṉāta ceytapiṉ, uyyā viḻumam tarum.

  6. Even our vengeance for a wanton injury results in our own unbearable sorrow. 74

  7. iṉṉā ceytārai oṟuttal avar nāṇa nal nayam ceytu, viṭal.

  8. The noblest revenge is to put the foe to the blush by our acts of kindness.

  9. aṟiviṉāṉ ākuvatu uṇṭō-piṟitiṉ nōy tam nōypōl pōṟṟākkaṭai?.

  10. What profiteth one’s reason, if one does not feel others’ sufferings as his own and guard against them?

  11. iṉṉā eṉat tāṉ uṇarntavai, tuṉṉāmai vēṇṭum, piṟaṉkaṇ ceyal.

  12. Avoid all that causes pain to others.

  13. eṉaittāṉum, eññāṉṟum, yārkkum, maṉattāṉ ām māṇā ceyyāmai talai.

  14. It is the supremest virtue not to commit at any time even slight injury to others.

  15. taṉ uyirkku iṉṉāmai tāṉ aṟivāṉ, eṉkolō, maṉ uyirkku iṉṉā ceyal?.

  16. How is it a man inflicts injury upon others knowing how painful it would be to himself?

75 319. piṟarkku iṉṉā muṟpakal ceyyiṉ, tamakku iṉṉā piṟpakal tāmē varum.
319. As the night follows day, evil that we do recoils on us.

  1. nōy ellām nōy ceytār mēlavām; nōy ceyyār, nōy iṉmai vēṇṭupavar.
  2. All sufferings befall those who inflict harm on others. Those who desire immunity from suffering never commit injury.
    1. kollāmai - 33. kollāmai -CHAPTER 33 CHAPTER 33 CHAPTER 33—NOT KILLING NOT KILLING NOT KILLING

  1. ‘aṟaviṉai yātu?’ eṉiṉ, kollāmai; kōṟal piṟa viṉai ellām tarum.

  2. If you ask what is the sum total of virtues, it is non-killing; killing begets sin.

  3. pakuttu uṇṭu, pal uyir ōmputal nūlōr tokuttavaṟṟuḷ ellām talai.

  4. All the scriptures emphasise the virtue of hospitality and the creed of nonviolence.

  5. oṉṟāka nallatu kollāmai; maṟṟu ataṉ piṉcārap poyyāmai naṉṟu.

  6. The crown of all virtues is non-violence. Next comes non-lying.

76 324. ’nallāṟu eṉappaṭuvatu yātu?’ eṉiṉ, yātu oṉṟum kollāmai cūḻum neṟi.
324. The path of rectitude is the path of non-violence.

  1. nilai añci nīttāruḷ ellām, kolai añcik kollāmai cūḻvāṉ, talai.

  2. Far greater than an ascetic who renounces the fleeting world is the follower of non-violence.

  3. kollāmai mēṟkoṇṭu oḻukuvāṉ vāḻnāḷmēl cellātu, uyir uṇṇum kūṟṟu.

  4. Yama, the Destroyer of life, never invades the realm where non-violence prevails.

  5. taṉ uyir nīppiṉum ceyyaṟka-tāṉ piṟitu iṉ uyir nīkkum viṉai.

  6. Do not commit any act of violence though your life is in peril.

  7. naṉṟu ākum ākkam peritu eṉiṉum, cāṉṟōrkkuk koṉṟu ākum ākkam kaṭai.

    1. The truly great scorn the riches acquired through slaughter.
  1. kolai viṉaiyar ākiya mākkaḷ pulai viṉaiyar, puṉmai terivār akattu. 77
    1. In the eyes of the discerning, men given to slaughter are but churls.
  1. ‘uyir uṭampiṉ nīkkiyār’ eṉpa-‘ceyir uṭampiṉ cellāt tī vāḻkkaiyavar’.
  2. Behold the Lazarus, he is guilty of acts of violence in his former birth.
    1. nilaiyāmai - 34. nilaiyāmai -CHAPTER 34 CHAPTER 34 CHAPTER 34—INSTABILITY INSTABILITY INSTABILITY

  1. nillātavaṟṟai nilaiyiṉa eṉṟu uṇarum pullaṟivu āṇmai kaṭai.

  2. It is contemptible folly to mistake the unstable for the stable.

  3. kūttāṭṭu avaikkuḻāttaṟṟē, peruñ celvam; pōkkum, atu viḷintaṟṟu.

  4. The flow of fortune is like the gathering of a crowd at a concert; its ebb is like the melting of the crowd at its close.

  5. aṟkā iyalpiṟṟuc celvam; atu peṟṟāl, aṟkupa āṅkē ceyal.

  6. Fortune is fickle; if you come by it delay not; put it to proper use.

  7. nāḷ eṉa oṉṟupōl kāṭṭi, uyir, īrum vāḷatu-uṇarvārp peṟiṉ. 78

  8. Time seems all laughter; but to the discerning it is a saw sawing away the life of men.

  9. nāc ceṟṟu, vikkuḷ mēlvārāmuṉ, nal viṉai mēṟceṉṟu ceyyappaṭum.

  10. Before hiccough arises and before the tongue is paralysed, do good that leads to salvation.

  11. ’nerunal uḷaṉ, oruvaṉ; iṉṟu illai!’ eṉṉum perumai uṭaittu, iv ulaku.

  12. Yesterday he was but to-day he is not; this is the glory of the earth.

  13. oru poḻutum vāḻvatu aṟiyār, karutupakōṭiyum alla, pala.

  14. One is not sure what awaits him the next moment; but he becomes a prey to a thousand and one thoughts.

  15. kuṭampai taṉittu oḻiyap puḷ paṟantaṟṟēuṭampoṭu uyiriṭai naṭpu.

    1. The attachment of life to the body is like that of a full-fledged bird flying from its

broken shell.

  1. uṟaṅkuvatu pōlum, cākkāṭu; uṟaṅki viḻippatu pōlum, piṟappu. 79

  2. Death is like sleep, birth is that awakening from sleep.

  3. pukkil amaintiṉṟukollō-uṭampiṉuḷ tuccil irunta uyirkku!.

  4. Why should the soul seek a temporary shelter in the perishable body? Is there not a durable habitation for it?

    1. tuṟ 35. tuṟavu -CHAPTER 35 CHAPTER 35— CHAPTER 35—RENUNCIATION RENUNCIATION RENUNCIATION

  1. yātaṉiṉ yātaṉiṉ nīṅkiyāṉ, nōtal ataṉiṉ ataṉiṉ ilaṉ.

  2. A man does not suffer pain from whatever things he has renounced.

  3. vēṇṭiṉ, uṇṭākat tuṟakka; tuṟantapiṉ, īṇṭu iyaṟpāla pala.

  4. There is endless joy in early renunciation.

  5. aṭal vēṇṭum, aintaṉ pulattai; viṭal vēṇṭum, vēṇṭiya ellām oruṅku.

  6. Subdue your senses and give up all your longings.

  7. iyalpu ākum, nōṉpiṟku oṉṟu iṉmai; uṭaimai mayal ākum, maṟṟum peyarttu.

  8. Renunciation is the mark of asceticism. Any clinging leads to one’s delusion. 80

  9. maṟṟum toṭarppāṭu evaṉkol? piṟappu aṟukkal uṟṟārkku uṭampum mikai.

    1. Why talk of other attachments; even our body is a hindrance.

  1. ‘yāṉ’, ‘eṉatu’, eṉṉum cerukku aṟuppāṉ vāṉōrkku uyarnta ulakam pukum.

  2. He enters the abode of the gods who lays the axe at ‘I’ and ‘mine.’

  3. paṟṟi viṭāa, iṭumpaikaḷ-paṟṟiṉaip paṟṟi, viṭāatavarkku.

  4. Sufferings seize men of desire.

  5. talaippaṭṭār, tīrat tuṟantār; mayaṅki valaippaṭṭār, maṟṟaiyavar.

  6. Salvation is for one of renunciation; others get entangled in endless births and deaths.

  7. paṟṟu aṟṟakaṇṇē piṟappu aṟukkum; maṟṟum nilaiyāmai kāṇappaṭum.

    1. Cut off all attachments; you cut off the tangle of life; otherwise you are caught.
  1. paṟṟuka, paṟṟu aṟṟāṉ paṟṟiṉai! ap paṟṟaip 81 paṟṟuka, paṟṟu viṭaṟku!.
  2. Cling fast to Him who is free from all desire. Seek Him for your freedom, from attachment.
    1. mey uṇ 36. mey uṇartal -CHAPTER 36 CHAPTER 36 CHAPTER 36—TRUE KNOWLEDGE TRUE KNOWLEDGE TRUE KNOWLEDGE
  1. poruḷ allavaṟṟaip poruḷ eṉṟu uṇarum maruḷāṉ ām, māṇāp piṟappu.
    1. Out of ignorance which mistakes things unreal for things real springs the

wretched cycle of births.

  1. iruḷ nīṅki iṉpam payakkum-maruḷ nīṅki mācu aṟu kāṭciyavarkku.

  2. Men of pure vision are led from darkness to light.

  3. aiyattiṉ nīṅkit teḷintārkku vaiyattiṉ vāṉam naṇiyatu uṭaittu.

  4. To men of unclouded wisdom heaven is nearer than earth.

  5. aiuṇarvu eytiyak kaṇṇum payam iṉṟēmey uṇarvu illātavarkku.

  6. What profits one’s perfect senses if one is not endowed with true knowledge.

  7. ep poruḷ et taṉmaittuāyiṉum, ap poruḷ 82 meypporuḷ kāṇpatu aṟivu.

  8. To track all things to their subtlest retreats is true knowledge.

  9. kaṟṟu īṇṭu meypporuḷ kaṇṭār talaippaṭuvar, maṟṟu īṇṭu vārā neṟi.

  10. Those who have learnt the truth never enter back to this world.

  11. ōrttu uḷḷam uḷḷatu uṇariṉ oru talaiyā, pērttu uḷḷavēṇṭā piṟappu.

  12. There is no fear of one’s re-birth if one seeks and finds the truth.

  13. piṟappu eṉṉum pētaimai nīṅka, ciṟappu eṉṉum cemporuḷ kāṇpatu aṟivu.

  14. Seek the truth to remove delusion; that is wisdom.

  15. cārpu uṇarntu, cārpu keṭa oḻukiṉ, maṟṟu aḻittuc cārtarā, cārtarum nōy.

    1. Seek the truth on which everything rests; you will be free from all the ills that

assail life.

  1. kāmam, vekuḷi, mayakkam, ivai mūṉṟaṉ nāmam keṭa, keṭum nōy.
  2. Wipe out the very names of lust, anger and delusion; you will be wiping out the pause of re-birth. 83
    1. avā aṟ 37. avā aṟuttal -CHAPTER 37 CHAPTER 37 CHAPTER 37—THE DESTRUCTION OF DESIRE THE DESTRUCTION OF DESIRE THE DESTRUCTION OF DESIRE

  1. ‘avā’ eṉpa-’ellā uyirkkum, eñ ñāṉṟum, tavāap piṟappu īṉum vittu’.

  2. The learned say desire is the eternal seed of life.

  3. vēṇṭuṅkāl, vēṇṭum piṟavāmai; maṟṟu atu vēṇṭāmai vēṇṭa, varum.

    1. Do you long for anything? Long for not being born again; this you can achieve if

you cease your desires.

  1. vēṇṭāmai aṉṉa viḻuc celvam īṇṭu illai; yāṇṭum aḵtu oppatu il.

  2. There is no greater possession than freedom from desire either here or in the world beyond.

  3. tūuymai eṉpatu avā iṉmai; maṟṟu atu vā aymai vēṇṭa, varum.

  4. What is purity of mind but absence of desire? It will follow if one burns for truth.

  5. aṟṟavar eṉpār avā aṟṟār; maṟṟaiyār aṟṟu āka aṟṟatu ilar.

  7. añcuvatu ōrum aṟaṉē; oruvaṉai vañcippatu ōrum avā.

  8. It is desire that seduces men into sin; Asceticism dreads desires.

  9. avāviṉai āṟṟa aṟuppiṉ, tavā viṉai tāṉvēṇṭum āṟṟāṉ varum.

  10. The desired path of virtue is open to one who kills desire.

  11. avā illārkku illākum tuṉpam; aḵtu uṇṭēl, tavāatu mēṉmēl varum.

  12. There is no sorrow for those who are free from desire. Endless sorrows befall men with desire.

  13. iṉpam iṭaiyaṟātu, īṇṭum-avā eṉṉum tuṉpattuḷ tuṉpam keṭiṉ.

  14. There is an eternal flow of life’s happiness when desire, the evil of ail evils, dies out.

  15. ārā iyaṟkai avā nīppiṉ, an nilaiyē pērā iyaṟkai tarum.

  16. Give up your insatiable longings; you will be conferring on yourself an eternal life.

    1. ūḻ-CHAPTER 38 CHAPTER 38 CHAPTER 38—FATE
  1. āku ūḻāl tōṉṟum, acaivu iṉmai; kaipporuḷ pōku ūḻāl tōṉṟum, maṭi.
    1. Out of fate springs perseverance which leads to one’s fortune. Out of fate

springs one’s indolence which leads to one’s ruin.

  1. pētaip paṭukkum, iḻavu ūḻ; aṟivu akaṟṟum, ākal ūḻ uṟṟakkaṭai.

  2. Fate makes fools of the wise. Fate makes folly pass for wisdom.

  3. nuṇṇiya nūl pala kaṟpiṉum, maṟṟum taṉ uṇmai aṟivē mikum.

  4. What if one is a man of subtle learning; one’s mind is swayed by fate.

  5. iru vēṟu, ulakattu iyaṟkai; tiru vēṟu; teḷḷiyar ātalum vēṟu.

  1. nallavai ellāam tīya ām; tīyavum nalla ām;-celvam ceyaṟku.
  2. Things favourable become adverse, and the unfavourable favourable.

86 376. pariyiṉum ākāvām, pāl alla; uyttuc coriyiṉum pōkā, tama.
376. One may lose one’s wealth however carefully one may guard it. One may not lose it though he flings it away. It is all ordained by fate.

  1. vakuttāṉ vakutta vakai allāl, kōṭi tokuttārkkum tuyttal aritu.

  2. Unless pre-ordained by the divine Disposer, even if a man did pile up a crore it would not be possible for him to enjoy it.

  3. tuṟappārmaṉ, tuppuravu illār-uṟaṟpāla ūṭṭā kaḻiyum eṉiṉ.

  4. The poor could easily renounce the world if fate were to refrain from visiting them with the curse of their past deeds.

  5. naṉṟu ām kāl nallavāk kāṇpavar, aṉṟu ām kāl allaṟpaṭuvatu evaṉ.

  6. Why worry about pain and pleasure? They are all the workings of fate.

  7. ūḻiṉ peruvali yā uḷa-maṟṟu oṉṟu cūḻiṉum, tāṉ muntuṟum.

  8. What is there so potent as Fate? Even if we devise some way of counteracting it, it takes us by surprise.

  6. Where people possess a king, who does not enforce justice, wealth does not confer more happiness than poverty.

  7. muṟai kōṭi maṉṉavaṉ ceyyiṉ, uṟai kōṭi ollātu, vāṉam peyal.

  8. Were the king to rule unjustly, the Heavens would withhold rains?

  9. ā payaṉ kuṉṟum; aṟutoḻilōr nūl maṟappar;- 123 kāvalaṉ kāvāṉ eṉiṉ.

    1. If the protecting monarch fails in his duties, the yield of cows will diminish and

Brahmans with their six duties will forget their Vedas.

    1. veruvanta ceyyāmai - 57. veruvanta ceyyāmai -CHAPTER 57 CHAPTER 57 CHAPTER 57—ON TYRANNY ON TYRANNY ON TYRANNY

  1. takkāṅku nāṭi, talaiccellā vaṇṇattāl ottāṅku oṟuppatu vēntu.

  2. A righteous king investigates and fittingly punishes the wrongdoer so that he may not repeat it.

  3. kaṭitu ōcci, mella eṟika-neṭitu ākkam nīṅkāmai vēṇṭupavar.

  4. If you wish enduring prosperity behave as if you punish excessively, but do it mildly.

  5. veruvanta ceytu oḻukum veṅkōlaṉ āyiṉ, oruvantam ollaik keṭum.

  6. The tyrant who terrifies his subjects will soon perish.

  7. ‘iṟai kaṭiyaṉ’ eṉṟu uraikkum iṉṉāc col vēntaṉ uṟai kaṭuki ollaik keṭum.

  8. That king whom people speak of as a tyrant will rapidly perish.

124 565. aruñ cevvi, iṉṉā mukattāṉ peruñ celvam pēey kaṇṭaṉṉatu uṭaittu.
565. The great wealth of a king who is inaccessible and assumes a fearful look, is no better than in the possession of a demon.

  1. kaṭuñ collaṉ, kaṇ ilaṉ āyiṉ, neṭuñ celvam nīṭu iṉṟi, āṅkē keṭum.

  2. The abundant wealth of a king who utters harsh words and puts on unkind looks will not last long.

  3. kaṭu moḻiyum, kaiyikanta taṇṭamum, vēntaṉ aṭu muraṇ tēykkum aram.

    1. Severity in speech and excess in punishment are like the file which removes his

capacity to destroy (his enemies).

  1. iṉattu āṟṟi, eṇṇāta vēntaṉ ciṉattu āṟṟic cīṟiṉ, ciṟukum tiru.

  2. The prosperity of a king who does not consult his advisers but makes them the victims of his fury will shrink.

  3. ceru vanta pōḻtil, ciṟai ceyyā vēntaṉ, veruvantu, veytu keṭum.

  4. If a king who has no fortress meets a foe, he will be ruined by fear.

125 570. kallārp piṇikkum, kaṭuṅkōl; atu allatu illai, nilakkup poṟai.
570. No burden is harder for the earth to bear than the cruel sceptre wielded by the unwise.

    1. kaṇṇ 58. kaṇṇōṭṭam -CHAPTER 58 CHAPTER 58 CHAPTER 58—ON KINDLINESS ON KINDLINESS ON KINDLINESS

  1. kaṇṇōṭṭam eṉṉum kaḻiperuṅ kārikai uṇmaiyāṉ, uṇṭu iv ulaku.

  2. The world exists because of the existence of the most beautiful virtue called kindliness.

  3. kaṇṇōṭṭattu uḷḷatu ulakiyal; aḵtu ilār uṇmai nilakkup poṟai.

  4. The world lives through kindliness; those who do not have it are a burden to the earth.

  5. paṇ eṉ ām, pāṭaṟku iyaipu iṉṟēl?-kaṇ eṉ ām, kaṇṇōṭṭam illāta kaṇ?.

  6. What is the use of a song that could not be enjoyed? Likewise, what is the use of the eyes that have no kindliness?

  7. uḷapōl mukattu evaṉ ceyyum-aḷaviṉāl kaṇṇōṭṭam illāta kaṇ.

  8. What is the use of one’s eyes if they do not beam with immeasurable love? 126

  9. kaṇṇiṟku aṇikalam kaṇṇōṭṭam; aḵtu iṉṟēl, puṇ eṉṟu uṇarappaṭum.

  10. Kindliness is the fitting ornament for the eyes. They are a sore, where it is absent.

  11. maṇṇoṭu iyainta marattu aṉaiyar-kaṇṇoṭu iyaintu, kaṇṇōṭātavar.

  12. Those whose eyes do not reflect love resemble trees that stand on the earth.

  13. kaṇṇōṭṭam illavar kaṇ ilar; kaṇ uṭaiyār kaṇṇōṭṭam iṉmaiyum il.

  14. Verily they are blind who have no kindly look.

  15. karumam citaiyāmal kaṇṇōṭa vallārkku urimai uṭaittu, iv ulaku.

  16. The world belongs to a king who can do his duty and yet be courteous.

  17. oṟuttāṟṟum paṇpiṉārkaṇṇum, kaṇṇōṭip poṟuttāṟṟum paṇpē talai.

  18. It behoves a king to put up with the doer of harm and even be kind to him.

  19. peyak kaṇṭum, nañcu uṇṭu amaivar-nayattakka 127 nākarikam vēṇṭupavar.

  20. Those who wish to acquire loveable urbanity will knowingly swallow even the poison served.

    1. oṟṟ 59. oṟṟu āṭal -CHAPTER 59 CHAPTER 59 CHAPTER 59—ON SPIES

  1. oṟṟum, urai cāṉṟa nūlum, ivai iraṇṭum teṟṟeṉka, maṉṉavaṉ kaṇ.

  2. Verily the two eyes of a king are espionage and the celebrated code of laws.

  3. ellārkkum ellām nikaḻpavai eññāṉṟum vallaṟital, vēntaṉ toḻil.

  4. A king’s duty is to get day to day knowledge of everything that happens.

  5. oṟṟiṉāṉ oṟṟi, poruḷ teriyā maṉṉavaṉ koṟṟam koḷak kiṭantatu il.

    1. The sure way of achieving success for a king is to get correct information from

spies.

  1. viṉaiceyvār, tam cuṟṟam, vēṇṭātār, eṉṟu āṅku aṉaivaraiyum ārāyvatu-oṟṟu.
    1. Espionage consists of watching all people, to wit, the king’s employees, his

relations and his enemies.

128 585. kaṭāa uruvoṭu kaṇ añcātu, yāṇṭum ukā amai vallatē-oṟṟu.
585. An able spy puts on undoubted disguise, does not fear when detected, and never reveals his purpose.

  1. tuṟantār paṭivattar āki iṟantu, ārāyntu, eṉ ceyiṉum cōrvu ilatu-oṟṟu.

  2. A spy in the guise of an ascetic should gather information however difficult and should never be tired whatever be the troubles.

  3. maṟaintavai kēṭka vaṟṟu āki, aṟintavai aiyappāṭu illatē-oṟṟu.

  4. A spy should secure knowledge of things secret and should have no doubt about his information.

  5. oṟṟu oṟṟit tanta poruḷaiyum, maṟṟum ōr oṟṟiṉāl oṟṟi, koḷal.

  6. One must get confirmed the information supplied by one spy, by that of another.

  7. oṟṟu oṟṟu uṇarāmai āḷka; uṭaṉ mūvar col tokka tēṟappaṭum.

  8. Let the engagement of one spy be not known to another. Accept the information supplied independently by three spies.

129 590. ciṟappu aṟiya oṟṟiṉkaṇ ceyyaṟka; ceyyiṉ, puṟappaṭuttāṉ ākum, maṟai.
590. Let not a king honour the spy publicly; for, by so doing he will be letting out his own secret.

–

    1. ūkkam uṭ 60. ūkkam uṭaimai -CHAPTER 60 HAPTER 60 HAPTER 60—ON EXERTION ON EXERTION ON EXERTION

  1. uṭaiyar eṉappaṭuvatu ūkkam; aḵtu illār uṭaiyatu uṭaiyarō, maṟṟu?.

  2. One’s real possession is one’s exertion. If one does not have it, can one be said to really possess anything else?

  3. uḷḷam uṭaimai uṭaimai; poruḷ uṭaimai nillātu nīṅkiviṭum.

  4. Exertion alone is one’s wealth; inconstant material wealth will pass away.

  5. ‘ākkam iḻantēm!’ eṉṟu allāvār-ūkkam oruvantam kaittu uṭaiyār.

  6. Those who possess constant exertion will not grieve over the loss of their wealth.

  7. ākkam atar viṉāyc cellum-acaivu ilā ūkkam uṭaiyāṉuḻai.

  8. Prosperity will discover a route to a person of undaunted will.

130 594. ākkam atar viṉāyc cellum-acaivu ilā ūkkam uṭaiyāṉuḻai.
595. The length of a watery plant is determined by the depth of the water. Likewise the greatness of a person is proportionate to the strength of his will power.

  1. uḷḷuvatu ellām uyarvu uḷḷal! maṟṟu atu taḷḷiṉum, taḷḷāmai nīrttu.

  2. In all acts and deeds, let exertion be one’s ideal. Even if it were unattainable, its presence is enough.

  3. citaiviṭattu olkār, uravōr;-putai ampiṉ paṭṭup pāṭu ūṉṟum kaḷiṟu.

  4. The elephant stands undaunted despite piercing arrows; so too, a person of strong will, will not get discouraged even in a losing concern.

  5. uḷḷam ilātavar eytār-‘ulakattu vaḷḷiyam’ eṉṉum cerukku.

  6. A man of no strong will, cannot win the esteem of the world for his action.

  7. pariyatu kūrṅ kōṭṭatu āyiṉum, yāṉai verūum, puli tākkuṟiṉ.

  8. Even the huge elephant with sharp tusks dreads the attacking tiger.

131 600. uram oruvaṟku uḷḷa veṟukkai; aḵtu illār maram; makkaḷ ātalē vēṟu.
600. One’s strength is one’s exertion. Without it persons are only trees in the form of men.

    1. maṭ 61. maṭi iṉmai -CHAPTER 61 CHAPTER 61 CHAPTER 61—AGAINST SLOTH AGAINST SLOTH AGAINST SLOTH

  1. kuṭi eṉṉum kuṉṟā viḷakkam, maṭi eṉṉum mācu ūra, māyntu keṭum.

  2. If sloth extends its darkness it will extinguish the lustrous lamp of one’s family.

  3. maṭiyai maṭiyā oḻukal-kuṭiyaik kuṭiyāka vēṇṭupavar!.

  4. Those who wish the esteem of their family should never encourage sloth.

  5. maṭi maṭik koṇṭu oḻukum pētai piṟanta kuṭi maṭiyum, taṉṉiṉum muntu.

  6. The family of the fool who hugs sloth in his own lap fades away before him.

  7. kuṭi maṭintu, kuṟṟam perukum-maṭi maṭintu, māṇṭa uñaṟṟu ilavarkku.

  8. Faults will be many among those who are devoid of exertion and will result in the ruin of their families.

132 605. neṭu nīr, maṟavi, maṭi, tuyil, nāṉkum keṭum nīrār kāmak kalaṉ.
605. Procrastination, carelessness, sluggardliness and sleep are the four boats fondly entered into by those who go to ruin.

  1. paṭi uṭaiyār paṟṟu amaintakkaṇṇum, maṭi uṭaiyār māṇ payaṉ eytal aritu.
    1. Even when the wealth of the rulers of all earth is within his reach, the slothful will

hardly derive any great benefit from it.

  1. iṭipurintu, eḷḷum col kēṭpar-maṭipurintu māṇṭa uñaṟṟu ilavar.

  2. Lovers of idleness with no praiseworthy exertion will be the butt of disgrace and will receive words of rebuke.

  3. maṭimai kuṭimaikkaṇ taṅkiṉ, taṉ oṉṉārkku aṭimai pukuttiviṭum.

  4. If sloth comes to stay in one’s family, it will make one the slave of one’s enemies.

  5. kuṭi, āṇmaiyuḷ vanta kuṟṟam, oruvaṉ maṭi āṇmai māṟṟa, keṭum.

    1. By conquering sloth, one can wipe out the reproach that has come over one’s

family.

133 610. maṭi ilā maṉṉavaṉ eytum-aṭi aḷantāṉ tāayatu ellām oruṅku.
610. All the universe once measured by God will be with the king of no sloth.

–

    1. āḷviṉai uṭaimai -CHAPTER 62 CHAPTER 62 CHAPTER 62—ON PERSEVERANCE ON PERSEVERANCE ON PERSEVERANCE

  1. arumai uṭaittu eṉṟu acāvāmai vēṇṭum; perumai muyaṟci tarum.

  2. “Do not give up (your task) saying ‘O’ It is very difficult." The art of doing it comes of exertion.

  3. viṉaikkaṇ viṉaikeṭal ōmpal-viṉaik kuṟai tīrntāriṉ tīrntaṉṟu, ulaku!.

  4. Do not give up your task in the middle; for the world will abandon those who leave their task unfinished.

  5. tāḷāṇmai eṉṉum takaimaikkaṇ taṅkiṟṟēvēḷāṇmai eṉṉum cerukku.

    1. The greatness which consists in helping others dwells in the virtue of

persevering effort.

  1. tāḷāṇmai illātāṉ vēḷāṇmai, pēṭi kai vāḷ āṇmai pōla, keṭum. 134

  2. The service of one with no persevering effort is vain like the sword wielded by a hermaphrodite.

  3. iṉpam viḻaiyāṉ, viṉai viḻaivāṉ taṉ kēḷir tuṉpam tuṭaittu ūṉṟum tūṇ.

  4. One who does not seek pleasure but delights in work will be a pillar of support to one’s relatives in their sorrow.

  5. muyaṟci-tiruviṉai ākkum; muyaṟṟu iṉmai iṉmai pukuttiviṭum.

    1. Exertion achieves wealth; absence of it brings on poverty.

  1. ‘maṭi uḷāḷ, mā mukaṭi’ eṉpa; maṭi ilāṉ tāḷ uḷāḷ, tāmaraiyiṉāḷ.

  2. Goddess of misfortune dwells in sloth; the Goddess of fortune lives in exertion.

  3. poṟi iṉmai yārkkum paḻi aṉṟu; aṟivu aṟintu, āḷviṉai iṉmai paḻi.

  4. Ill-luck is no disgrace; but it is a disgrace if one does not exert himself as to what should be done.

  5. teyvattāṉ ākātueṉiṉum, muyaṟci taṉ mey varuttak kūli tarum.

  6. Though fate should ordain failure, bodily exertion will yield its own reward. 135

  7. ūḻaiyum uppakkam kāṇpar-ulaivu iṉṟit tāḻātu uñaṟṟupavar.

  8. Those who labour hard, undaunted by obstacles will overcome destiny.

    1. iṭukkaṇaḻiyāmai -CHAPTER 63 CHAPTER 63 CHAPTER 63—ON COURAGE ON COURAGE ON COURAGE

  1. iṭukkaṇ varuṅkāl nakuka! ataṉai aṭuttu ūrvatu aḵtu oppatu il.

  2. Laugh over your obstacles; nothing like it to push them further and further.

  3. veḷḷattu aṉaiya iṭumpai, aṟivu uṭaiyāṉ uḷḷattiṉ uḷḷa, keṭum.

  4. Troubles like a flood will be overcome by a courageous thought rising in the minds of the wise.

  5. iṭumpaikku iṭumpai paṭuppar-iṭumpaikku iṭumpai paṭāatavar.

  6. The courageous will be causing sorrow to sorrow itself.

  7. maṭutta vāy ellām pakaṭu aṉṉāṉ uṟṟa iṭukkaṇ iṭarppāṭu uṭaittu.

  8. Just as the buffalo drags a cart through miry depth, one who fights on will overcome his difficulties. 136

  9. aṭukki variṉum, aḻivu ilāṉ uṟṟa iṭukkaṇ iṭukkaṇ paṭum.

  10. The troubles of one who braves a series of adversity wear out and disappear.

  11. ‘aṟṟēm!’ eṉṟu allaṟpaṭupavō-‘peṟṟēm!’ eṉṟu ōmputal tēṟṟātavar.

    1. Will those who do not during prosperity exultingly say “we are rich”, cry out

(during adversity) “Oh, we are destitute”?

  1. ‘ilakkam, uṭampu iṭumpaikku’ eṉṟu, kalakkattaik kaiyāṟāk koḷḷātām, mēl.

  2. The great know that the body is ever the target of trouble and will not regard trouble as trouble at all.

  3. iṉpam viḻaiyāṉ, ‘iṭumpai iyalpu’ eṉpāṉ, tuṉpam uṟutal ilaṉ.

  4. He who never gives way to sorrow, will not long for pleasure; he will regard trouble as quite natural.

  5. iṉpattuḷ iṉpam viḻaiyātāṉ, tuṉpattuḷ tuṉpam uṟutal ilaṉ.

  6. He who does seek for pleasure in pleasure will not be vexed in sorrow.

137 630. iṉṉāmai iṉpam eṉak koḷiṉ, ākum, taṉ oṉṉār viḻaiyum ciṟappu.

    1. One who regards trouble as pleasure will gain the elevation which his enemies

desire (for themselves).

SECTION II. LIMBS OF THE STATE SECTION II. LIMBS OF THE STATE

    1. amaiccu - 64. amaiccu -CHAPTER 64 CHAPTER 64 CHAPTER 64—ON MINISTERS ON MINISTERS ON MINISTERS

  1. karuviyum, kālamum, ceykaiyum, ceyyum aruviṉaiyum, māṇṭatu-amaiccu.

  2. He is the minister who, finds out the means, the time, the deed and its full accomplishment.

  3. vaṉkaṇ, kuṭikāttal, kaṟṟu aṟital, āḷviṉaiyōṭu aintuṭaṉ māṇṭatu-amaiccu.

  4. A minister should have five qualities; tenacity of purpose, birth in a respectable family, welfare of the people, profound learning and perseverance.

  5. pirittalum, pēṇikkoḷalum, pirintārp poruttalum, vallatu-amaiccu.

  6. A minister must be able to separate a foe from his ally, befriend allies and reunite separated allies.

138 634. teritalum, tērntu ceyalum, orutalaiyāc collalum vallatu-amaiccu.
634. A minister should study the consequences of an act and carry it successfully by a decisive speech.

  1. aṟaṉ aṟintu, āṉṟu amainta collāṉ, eññāṉṟum tiṟaṉ aṟintāṉ, tērccit tuṇai.
    1. He is a helpful counselor who is righteous and considerate in his speech, and

always knows how to act.

  1. matinuṭpam nūlōṭu uṭaiyārkku ati nuṭpam yā uḷa, muṉ niṟpavai?.

  2. To a keen intellect combined with learning no difficulty stands in the way.

  3. ceyaṟkai aṟintakkaṭaittum, ulakattu iyaṟkai aṟintu, ceyal!.

  4. Even though you know the rules, act in conformity with the world opinion.

  5. aṟi koṉṟu, aṟiyāṉ eṉiṉum, uṟuti uḻaiyiruntāṉ kūṟal kaṭaṉ.

  6. Though a king listens not to wise words it is the duty of the minister to speak firmly to him.

  7. paḻutu eṇṇum mantiriyiṉ, pakkattuḷ tev ōr 139 eḻupatu kōṭi uṟum.

    1. A treacherous minister by the king’s side is equal to seventy crores of enemies.
  1. muṟaippaṭac cūḻntum, muṭivilavē ceyvartiṟappāṭu ilāatavar.
  2. Ministers who have no requisite ability will leave a task unfinished though well begun.
    1. col vaṉ 65. col vaṉmai -CHAPTER 65 CHAPTER 65 CHAPTER 65—ON GOOD SPEECH ON GOOD SPEECH ON GOOD SPEECH
  1. ’nā nalam’ eṉṉum nalaṉ uṭaimai; an nalam yā nalattu uḷḷatūum aṉṟu.
    1. The virtue of good speech is greater than all the other good qualities found in

one.

  1. ākkamum, kēṭum, ataṉāl varutalāl, kāttu ōmpal, colliṉkaṇ cōrvu.

  2. As I both prosperity and ruin are caused by words, a minister must guard against imperfection in his speech.

  3. kēṭṭārp piṇikkum takai avāy, kēḷārum vēṭpa, moḻivatu ām-col.

    1. The minister must use such words as have the effect of strengthening the

approval of those who agree and differ. 140

  1. tiṟaṉ aṟintu colluka, collai; aṟaṉum poruḷum ataṉiṉ ūṅku il.

  2. Speak having regard to one’s capacity to listen; for there is no greater virtue nor wealth than that.

  3. colluka collai-piṟitu ōr col ac collai vellum col iṉmai aṟintu.

  4. Speak out what you have to say only after knowing that your own argument will not be turned against you.

  5. vēṭpat tām colli, piṟar col payaṉ kōṭal māṭciyiṉ mācu aṟṟār kōḷ.

    1. A good minister wins the approval of the listener by persuasive speech.

  1. colal vallaṉ, cōrvu ilaṉ, añcāṉ, avaṉai ikal vellal yārkkum aritu.

  2. A clever speaker is neither tired nor fearful; none can defeat him in a debate.

  3. viraintu toḻil kēṭkum ñālam-nirantu iṉitu collutal vallārp peṟiṉ.

    1. Cogent reasoning and soft speech can bring the people over to one’s side.

141 649. pala collak kāmuṟuvar maṉṟa- mācu aṟṟa cila collal tēṟṟātavar.

    1. Those who cannot say a few words correctly will evince a desire to speak much.
  1. iṇar ūḻttum nāṟā malar aṉaiyar-kaṟṟatu uṇara virittu uraiyātār.
  2. Those who cannot explain well what they have learnt resemble the odourless flowers with their petals open.
    1. viṉ 66. viṉait tūyma ait tūyma ait tūymai -CHAPTER 66 CHAPTER 66 CHAPTER 66—ON PURITY IN ACTION ON PURITY IN ACTION ON PURITY IN ACTION
  1. tuṇai nalam ākkam tarūum; viṉai nalam vēṇṭiya ellām tarum.
    1. A man’s friends bring prosperity to him; but his good acts fetch him his wish.
  1. eṉṟum oruvutal vēṇṭum-pukaḻoṭu naṉṟi payavā viṉai.
    1. That deed must always be discarded which does not promote virtue and

  1. ōotal vēṇṭum, oḷi māḻkum ceyviṉai- ‘āatum!’ eṉṉumavar.
    1. Those who wish to become great must always avoid deeds which darken the

lustre of their reputation.

142 654. iṭukkaṇ paṭiṉum, iḷivanta ceyyārnaṭukku aṟṟa kāṭciyavar.
654. Even adversity does not prompt men of unswerving purity to do mean things.

  1. ’eṟṟu!’ eṉṟu iraṅkuva ceyyaṟka; ceyvāṉēl, maṟṟu aṉṉa ceyyāmai naṉṟu.
    1. Desist from deeds which you may regret later; but if you once happen to do

such a deed, repeat it not.

  1. īṉṟāḷ paci kāṇpāṉ āyiṉum, ceyyaṟka cāṉṟōr paḻikkum viṉai.
    1. Though you find your mother starving, do not do anything which will be

condemned by the great.

  1. paḻi malaintu eytiya ākkattiṉ, cāṉṟōr kaḻi nalkuravē talai.

  2. Better the poverty adopted by the great than the wealth resulting from sin.

  3. kaṭinta kaṭintu orār ceytārkku avaitām muṭintālum, pīḻai tarum.

  4. Those who do knowingly forbidden things will suffer in the end, although they may succeed in doing them.

  5. aḻak koṇṭa ellām aḻap pōm; iḻappiṉum, 143 piṟpayakkum, naṟpālavai.

  6. What is secured by causing tears to others will be lost with tears. But good deeds will result in good later.

  7. calattāl poruḷ ceytu ēmākkal-pacu maṇkalattuḷ nīr peytu, irīiyaṟṟu.

  8. A minister who promotes his king’s resources by fraud is like one who tries to store up water in a pot of unburnt clay.

    1. viṉ 67. viṉait tiṭpam -CHAPTER 67—ON RESOLUTENESS ON RESOLUTENESS ON RESOLUTENESS

  1. viṉait tiṭpam eṉpatu oruvaṉ maṉat tiṭpam; maṟṟaiya ellām piṟa.

  2. Determination in action is one’s resolution. All others are nothing.

  3. ūṟu orāl, uṟṟapiṉ olkāmai, iv iraṇṭiṉ āṟu eṉpar-āyntavar kōḷ.

  6. A clever minister publishes a deed after its completion; if it becomes public in the intermediate stage, it will end in trouble.

144 664. collutal yārkkum eḷiya; ariya ām, colliya vaṇṇam ceyal.
664. It is easy for one to say, but it is difficult to do it in the said manner.

  1. vīṟu eyti māṇṭār viṉait tiṭpam, vēntaṉkaṇ ūṟu eyti, uḷḷappaṭum.

  1. kalaṅkātu kaṇṭa viṉaikkaṇ, tuḷaṅkātu tūkkam kaṭintu ceyal.

    1. viṉ 68. viṉai ceyal vakai ai ceyal vakai ai ceyal vakai -CHAPTER 68 CHAPTER 68 CHAPTER 68—ON THE MEANS OF ACTION ON THE MEANS OF ACTION ON THE MEANS OF ACTION

146 674. viṉai, pakai eṉṟu iraṇṭiṉ eccam, niṉaiyuṅkāl, tī eccam pōlat teṟum.

  2. Do a thing after carefully deliberating on five things; resources, means, the time, the nature of the deed, and the place.

  3. muṭivum, iṭaiyūṟum, muṟṟiyāṅku eytum paṭupayaṉum, pārttuc ceyal!.

  5. ceyviṉai ceyvāṉ ceyalmuṟai, av viṉai uḷ aṟivāṉ uḷḷam koḷal.

  1. viṉaiyāṉ viṉai ākkikkōṭal-naṉai kavuḷ yāṉaiyāl yāṉai yāttaṟṟu.
    1. Use one act to achieve another just as one wild elephant is used to capture
